The Legacy of Shams al-Aimmah al-Hulwani: Teacher of al-Sarakhsi
Biographical note on al-Hulwani and his works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly lineage of al-Hulwani and explain the significance of his unprinted works in the transmission of Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Hulwani’s works are unprinted but foundational; al-Sarakhsi’s Mabsut built upon them.

This passage introduces us to a key figure in the Hanafi tradition: Shams al-Aimmah al-Hulwani. He was the teacher of the famous al-Sarakhsi, author of al-Mabsut. Understanding al-Hulwani helps us map the chain of knowledge transmission and the reliance on manuscripts in early Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person
Find al-Hulwani's full name, date of death, and nisba. The passage gives: Shams al-Aimmah Abdul Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari al-Hulwani (d. 448 AH).
The title 'Shams al-Aimmah' is shared by several Hanafi scholars.
2
Identify his role
Al-Hulwani is described as a Hanafi jurist of the fifth century and the teacher of Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi.
3
List his works
The passage lists three works: Al-Mabsut, Al-Fatawa, and Sharh Adab al-Qadi (a commentary on Abu Yusuf's work).
All are unprinted, meaning they survive only in manuscript form.
4
Note their status
The fact that al-Hulwani's works are unprinted explains why later scholars like al-Sarakhsi, whose Mabsut is printed, became more widely known.
5
Reflect on transmission
Consider how the teacher-student relationship ensures continuity and authority. Al-Hulwani's works are transmitted through al-Sarakhsi, and later scholars rely on al-Sarakhsi's version.
This illustrates the concept of riwayah (transmission) in Hanafi scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۱۲ - مبسوط شمس الأئمة الحلواني : لشمس الأئمة عبد العزيز ابن أحمد البخاری، الحلواني رحمه الله (المتوفى سنة ٤٤٨هـ) حنفى من فقهاء القرن الخامس والحلواني نسبة إلى حلوى " فلذلك ينسب "الحلواني " أيضاً - أستاذ شمس الأئمة السرخسی رحمه الله وكتبه غير مطبوعة، وهي : 1 - المبسوط . ٢- الفتاوى . -- شرح أدب القاضي لأبي يوسف رحمه الله .
112 Mabsut Shams al-Aimmah al-Hulwani: By Shams al-Aimmah Abdul Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari, al-Hulwani, may Allah have mercy on him (died 448 AH), a Hanafi from the jurists of the fifth century. Al-Hulwani is a nisba to 'Halwa', therefore also pronounced 'al-Hulwani'. He was the teacher of Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi, may Allah have mercy on him. His books are unprinted, namely: 1. Al-Mabsut. 2. Al-Fatawa. 3. Sharh Adab al-Qadi of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage provides brief biographical information about Imam al-Hulwani, the teacher of al-Sarakhsi. It lists his three known works, which remain unprinted. This is important for understanding the transmission of Hanafi knowledge: al-Hulwani's works are foundational but not widely available in print, so later scholars relied on al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut which built upon them.

Key Terms
شمس الأئمة الحلواني (Shams al-Aimmah al-Hulwani): Title of Imam Abdul Aziz al-Bukhari al-Hulwani, a great Hanafi jurist and teacher of al-Sarakhsi.

The Shared Title 'Shams al-Aimmah'
A biographical list of Hanafi scholars sharing an honorific title

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the multiple Hanafi scholars who bore the title 'Shams al-Aimmah' and explain why this matters for correctly attributing fatwas.

Core Idea
The title 'Shams al-Aimmah' was shared by several Hanafi masters — never assume it refers to one scholar alone.

In Hanafi literature, you will encounter the honorific 'Shams al-Aimmah' (Sun of the Imams) attached to different scholars. This passage from Rasm al-Mufti clarifies that the title belongs to a group of our imams, not just one. Understanding this prevents confusion when reading fatwas or biographical notes.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of scholars
Carefully go through each name mentioned. Note the names: al-Hulwani, al-Sarakhsi, al-Kardari, al-Zaranjari (father and son), al-Bayhaqi, and al-Uzjandi.
Some names include kunya or nisba — these are identifiers.
2
Identify teacher-student links
The passage notes that al-Sarakhsi was a student of al-Hulwani. Other relationships may be inferred: al-Zaranjari and his son.
Knowing these links helps contextualize their works.
3
Understand the shared title
The title 'Shams al-Aimmah' was a high honor, but not unique. Recognize that multiple accomplished scholars could hold it.
This is similar to 'Imam al-Haramayn' used for al-Juwayni and others.
4
Apply to fatwa work
When you see 'Shams al-Aimmah' qala... in a text, check the context (e.g., century, region, teacher) to determine which scholar it refers to.
Mistaking the identity can lead to incorrect attribution.
5
Note the variant title 'Shams al-Islam'
The passage adds that al-Uzjandi is also called 'Shams al-Islam'. Be aware of interchangeable honorifics.
Always verify from reliable sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة : لقب بـ شمس الأئمة جماعة من أئمتنا، منهم: شمس الأئمة الحلواني، ومنهم تلميذه شمس الأئمة السرخسي، ومنهم شمس الأئمة محمد عبد الله الكردري ومنهم شمس الأئمة بكر بن محمد الزرنجرى، ومنهم ابنه شمس الأئمة عماد الدين عمرو بن بكر بن محمد الزرنجرى، ومنهم شمس الأئمة البيهقي، ومنهم شمس الأئمة الأوز جندى واسمه محمود، وكثيراً ما يلقب بـ شمس الإسلام" . كذا في حاشية نوح
Benefit: The title 'Shams al-Aimmah' was given to a group of our imams, including: Shams al-Aimmah al-Hulwani, his student Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi, Shams al-Aimmah Muhammad Abdullah al-Kardari, Shams al-Aimmah Bakr ibn Muhammad al-Zaranjari, his son Shams al-Aimmah Imad al-Din Amr ibn Bakr ibn Muhammad al-Zaranjari, Shams al-Aimmah al-Bayhaqi, and Shams al-Aimmah al-Uzjandi whose name is Mahmud. Often he is also titled 'Shams al-Islam'. This is from the marginalia of Nuh.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the honorific 'Shams al-Aimmah' (Sun of the Imams) was applied to several prominent Hanafi scholars, not just one. It lists seven individuals. This helps students avoid confusion when encountering the same title in different contexts. The note also mentions that sometimes the title 'Shams al-Islam' is used interchangeably.

Key Terms
شمس الأئمة (Shams al-Aimmah): An honorific title meaning 'Sun of the Imams', given to several leading Hanafi scholars.
شمس الإسلام (Shams al-Islam): An alternative title for al-Uzjandi, also meaning 'Sun of Islam'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many scholars are listed as bearers of the title 'Shams al-Aimmah' in this passage?
A) Three
B) Five
C) Seven
D) Nine

Key Takeaway
The title 'Shams al-Aimmah' was borne by multiple Hanafi scholars; always verify the specific individual through context.

Al-Mabsut al-Kabir of Bakr Khwarizmi
Biographical entry introducing a Hanafi work and its author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, full name, and key work 'Al-Mabsut al-Kabir', and distinguish it from the similarly named work by al-Sarakhsi.

Core Idea
Al-Mabsut al-Kabir by Bakr Khwarizmi is a major Hanafi fiqh reference, distinct from al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut.

This passage introduces a foundational Hanafi fiqh work, Al-Mabsut al-Kabir, authored by the prominent Transoxianan scholar Bakr Khwarizmi. Understanding the identity of this work and its author is crucial for any mufti, as it is frequently cited in fatwa literature. The passage also includes an important note to avoid confusion with another scholar also known as Khwarizmi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's full name and death date
Locate the complete name of the author (Abi Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bukhari) and his death year (483 AH). This establishes his scholarly identity and period.
Death dates help contextualize a work within the Hanafi tradition.
2
Identify the work and its alternate names
Find the main work being described, Al-Mabsut al-Kabir, and note its other designations: Mabsut Khwarizmi, Mabsut al-Bakri, Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam.
Knowing alternate names prevents confusion when encountering different citations.
3
Trace the author's scholarly lineage
The text mentions that Bakr Khwarizmi is the nephew (son of sister) of the judge Imam Abi Thabit Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari. This connects him to a known Hanafi authority.
Lineage often indicates transmission of knowledge and madhhab affiliation.
4
Distinguish from another 'Khwarizmi'
Read the concluding note: Allamah Badr al-Din al-Kardari (died 651 AH) is also known as Khwarizmi. He is a different scholar and author of a different work. Note the shared nickname but different century and achievements.
The note prevents students from attributing the wrong work to the wrong scholar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۱۳ المبسوط الكبير : لشيخ الإسلام أبي بكر محمد بن الحسين بن محمد ابن الحسين البخاري (المتوفى سنة ٤٨٣ هـ ) يعرف بـ بكر خواهرزاده : وهو ابن أخت القاضي الإمام أبي ثابت محمد بن أحمد البخارى كان من عظماء ما وراء النهر، مشاهير كتب الفتاوى مشحونة بذكره. وله المختصر"، و "التجنيس"، و "المبسوط" المعروف بـ مبسوط خواهرزاده ويقال له : "المبسوط الكبير"، و "مبسوط البكري"، و مبسوط شيخ الإسلام"، وهو في خمسة عشر مجلداً.
وإن شئت الزيادة فراجع " شيخ الإسلام بكر المعروف بخواهرزاده فى الأعلام. ملحوظة : ويعرف بخواهرزاده العلامة بدر الدين محمد بن محمود الكردری
المتوفى ٦٥١هـ ، ابن أخت شمس الأئمة محمد بن عبد الستار الكردري أيضاً .
113 Al-Mabsut al-Kabir: By Shaykh al-Islam Abi Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bukhari (died 483 AH), known as Bakr Khwarizmi. He was the nephew (son of sister) of the judge Imam Abi Thabit Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari. He was among the great scholars of Transoxiana; famous fatwa books are filled with his mention. He authored Al-Mukhtasar, Al-Tajnis, and Al-Mabsut known as Mabsut Khwarizmi, also called Al-Mabsut al-Kabir, Mabsut al-Bakri, and Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam. It is in fifteen volumes. If you wish more, refer to "Shaykh al-Islam Bakr known as Khwarizmi" in al-A'lam. Note: Also known as Khwarizmi is Allamah Badr al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Kardari (died 651 AH), also the nephew of Shams al-Aimmah Muhammad ibn Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage introduces another major Hanafi work, Al-Mabsut al-Kabir by Bakr Khwarizmi. It distinguishes this book from al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut. The author is a prominent figure from Transoxiana. The note at the end clarifies that there is another scholar also known as Khwarizmi, preventing confusion.

Key Terms
المبسوط الكبير (Al-Mabsut al-Kabir): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by Bakr Khwarizmi in fifteen volumes, also known as Mabsut Khwarizmi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the author of Al-Mabsut al-Kabir?
A) Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi
B) Bakr Khwarizmi
C) Shams al-Aimmah al-Hulwani
D) Badr al-Din al-Kardari

Key Takeaway
Al-Mabsut al-Kabir is a major Hanafi fiqh reference by Bakr Khwarizmi (d. 483 AH), and it is essential to distinguish it from the similarly named work by al-Sarakhsi and from another scholar also called Khwarizmi.

Al-Tamartashi and His Tanwir al-Absar
Biographical description of al-Tamartashi and his work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Tamartashi's key teachers and state the significance of his work Tanwir al-Absar in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Tamartashi’s Tanwir al-Absar is a foundational matn for Hanafi fatwa, studied under Zayn ibn Nujaym.

This passage introduces us to the author of one of the most widely used Hanafi matn texts: Tanwir al-Absar. Understanding the background of the author and his teachers helps us appreciate the transmission and authority of the work. Al-Tamartashi's biography reveals a scholar deeply rooted in the Hanafi tradition despite studying under Shafi'i teachers, illustrating the interconnectedness of Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Trace the Lineage and Nisba
Read the full name and geographical nisba. Note that 'al-Tamartashi' may refer to a village or a grandfather. This helps identify the scholarly networks.
The text clarifies both possibilities.
2
Identify Teachers and Their Significance
List the teachers mentioned: Shams al-Mashriqi (Shafi'i), Zayn ibn Nujaym (Hanafi), Amin al-Dawla, and Ali ibn al-Hadha'i. Note that Zayn ibn Nujaym is a major Hanafi authority (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq).
This shows al-Tamartashi studied under both Shafi'i and Hanafi scholars.
3
Assess Scholarly Reputation
From al-Muhibbi's description, note that he was considered the chief of jurists of his time, with strong memory and vast knowledge. This establishes the reliability of his works.
Such praise indicates the high standing of his texts.
4
Understand the Importance of Tanwir al-Absar
Recognize that this matn became a standard reference for Hanafi fiqh and fatwa. Its conciseness made it popular for teaching and memorization.
Knowing the author's background adds weight to the text's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١١٤ - متن التنوير للتمرتاشي : وهو تنوير الأبصار وجامع البحار . للعلامة محمد بن عبد الله بن أحمد الخطيب بن محمد الخطيب بن إبراهيم الخطيب ابن محمد الخطيب التمرتاشي، الغزى الحنفى ولد بغزة هاشم سنة ٩٣٩هـ الموافق ١٥٣٣م . فيقال له :الغزى وهى كما في القاموس : بلدة بفلسطين. ولد بها الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله ومات بها هاشم بن عبد مناف . وقد يقال له : التمرتاشي.
وهو نسبة إلى تمرتاش (بضمتين وسكون الراء قرية من قرى خوارزم وقال الشامي الأقرب أنه نسبة إلى جده تمرتاشي . أخذ ببلده أنواع الفنون عن مفتى الشافعية بغزة الشمس محمد ابن المشرقى الغزى، ثم رحل إلى القاهرة أربع مرات، وتفقه بها على الشيخ الإمام زين ابن نجيم صاحب البحر" ، والإمام الكبير أمين الدولة بن عبد العال، وأخذ عن المولى على بن الحذائي قاضي القضاة بمصر. ورجع إلى بلاده وقد كان رأس في العلوم وقصده الناس للفتوى . قال المحبى فى خلاصة الأثر : رأس الفقهاء في عصره، كان إماماً فاضلا كبيراً ، حسن السمت جميل ،الطريقة قوى الحافظة، كثير الاطلاع وبالجملة فلم يبق فى آخر أمره من يساويه فى الدرجة . وقد ألف التأليف العجيبة المتقنة :
114 Matn al-Tanwir by al-Tamartashi: It is Tanwir al-Absar wa Jami' al-Bihar. By Allamah Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Ahmad al-Khatib ibn Muhammad al-Khatib ibn Ibrahim al-Khatib ibn Muhammad al-Khatib al-Tamartashi, al-Ghazzi al-Hanafi. He was born in Ghazza Hashim in 939 AH / 1533 CE. He is called al-Ghazzi, and as in al-Qamus: a town in Palestine. Imam al-Shafi'i was born there and Hashim ibn Abd Manaf died there. He is also called al-Tamartashi. It is a nisba to Tamartash (with two dammas and sukun on ra', a village of Khwarazm; al-Shami said the more correct is that it is a nisba to his grandfather Tamartashi. He studied various sciences in his country under the Mufti of the Shafi'is in Gaza, Shams Muhammad ibn al-Mashriqi al-Ghazzi. Then he traveled to Cairo four times and studied fiqh there under Shaykh Imam Zayn ibn Nujaym, author of al-Bahr, and the great Imam Amin al-Dawla ibn Abd al-Aal. He also studied under Mawla Ali ibn al-Hadha'i, the chief judge of Egypt. He returned to his country, having become a leader in the sciences, and people came to him for fatwa. Al-Muhibbi said in Khulasat al-Athar: He was the chief of the jurists of his time; he was a great, virtuous imam, of good demeanor, beautiful conduct, strong memory, vast knowledge; in short, at the end of his life none equaled his rank. He authored amazing, precise works.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a detailed biography of Allamah al-Tamartashi, the author of Tanwir al-Absar, a concise Hanafi fiqh text (matn). It describes his lineage, his teachers (including Zayn ibn Nujaym, the author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq), his travels, and his scholarly status. The text also clarifies the nisba 'al-Tamartashi' and mentions that Gaza is also associated with Imam al-Shafi'i. This work is a standard reference in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
تنوير الأبصار (Tanwir al-Absar): A succinct Hanafi fiqh matn (text) by al-Tamartashi, often commented upon.
زين بن نجيم (Zayn ibn Nujaym): A major Hanafi jurist, author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, teacher of al-Tamartashi.
الغزي (al-Ghazzi): Nisba referring to Gaza, a town in Palestine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which Hanafi scholar did al-Tamartashi study fiqh in Cairo?
A) Imam al-Shafi'i
B) Zayn ibn Nujaym
C) Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi
D) Amin al-Dawla ibn Abd al-Aal

Key Takeaway
Al-Tamartashi was a leading Hanafi jurist whose concise matn Tanwir al-Absar became central for iftaa, studied under Zayn ibn Nujaym and other scholars.

Key Hanafi Texts Cited in the Sharh
Enumeration of five Hanafi reference books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify five key Hanafi reference works, name their authors, and explain their importance for fatwa.

Core Idea
Knowing Hanafi texts by name and author is foundational for navigating fatwa sources.

This passage from Ibn Mustafa al-Rumi's sharh on al-Durar wa al-Ghurar lists five essential Hanafi fiqh texts. These works form the backbone of later Hanafi fatwa practice. Memorizing their names, authors, and characteristics will help you locate rulings and understand the chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify each text by name
List the five texts mentioned: al-Mabsut al-Kabir, Tanwir al-Absar, Ghurar al-Ahkam, al-Mujarrad, and Majma' al-Bahrayn.
Some texts have multiple names; note the most common ones.
2
Match each text to its author
Associate each work with its author: Bakr Khwarizmi (al-Mabsut), al-Timurtashi (Tanwir), Mulla Khusraw (Ghurar), al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (al-Mujarrad), Ibn al-Sa'ati (Majma').
Also note any alternative names for the authors.
3
Note the key feature of each work
Observe unique characteristics: al-Mabsut is 15 volumes; Tanwir is a precise matn; Ghurar is paired with al-Durar; al-Mujarrad is by a direct student of Abu Hanifa; Majma' compiles Quduri's al-Manzoomah.
These features determine how each text is used in iftaa.
4
Understand the text's role in fatwa
Recognize that these are authoritative sources; knowing them allows a mufti to quickly locate reliable rulings.
Al-Mabsut and Tanwir are particularly widely cited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتب الواردة في الشرح ابن مصطفى الرومى الحنفى أفندى المتوفى ۱۰۷۰هـ على الدرر والغرر فى فصل المهر .
۱۱۳ المبسوط الكبير : لشيخ الإسلام أبي بكر محمد بن الحسين بن محمد ابن الحسين البخاري (المتوفى سنة ٤٨٣ هـ ) يعرف بـ بكر خواهرزاده : وهو ابن أخت القاضي الإمام أبي ثابت محمد بن أحمد البخارى كان من عظماء ما وراء النهر، مشاهير كتب الفتاوى مشحونة بذكره. وله المختصر"، و "التجنيس"، و "المبسوط" المعروف بـ مبسوط خواهرزاده ويقال له : "المبسوط الكبير"، و "مبسوط البكري"، و مبسوط شيخ الإسلام"، وهو في خمسة عشر مجلداً.
وإن شئت الزيادة فراجع " شيخ الإسلام بكر المعروف بخواهرزاده فى الأعلام. ملحوظة : ويعرف بخواهرزاده العلامة بدر الدين محمد بن محمود الكردری
المتوفى ٦٥١هـ ، ابن أخت شمس الأئمة محمد بن عبد الستار الكردري أيضاً .
١١٤ - متن التنوير للتمرتاشي : وهو تنوير الأبصار وجامع البحار . للعلامة محمد بن عبد الله بن أحمد الخطيب بن محمد الخطيب بن إبراهيم الخطيب ابن محمد الخطيب التمرتاشي، الغزى الحنفى ولد بغزة هاشم سنة ٩٣٩هـ الموافق ١٥٣٣م . فيقال له :الغزى وهى كما في القاموس : بلدة بفلسطين. ولد بها الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله ومات بها هاشم بن عبد مناف . وقد يقال له : التمرتاشي.
وهو نسبة إلى تمرتاش (بضمتين وسكون الراء قرية من قرى خوارزم وقال الشامي الأقرب أنه نسبة إلى جده تمرتاشي . أخذ ببلده أنواع الفنون عن مفتى الشافعية بغزة الشمس محمد ابن المشرقى الغزى، ثم رحل إلى القاهرة أربع مرات، وتفقه بها على الشيخ الإمام زين ابن نجيم صاحب البحر" ، والإمام الكبير أمين الدولة بن عبد العال، وأخذ عن المولى على بن الحذائي قاضي القضاة بمصر. ورجع إلى بلاده وقد كان رأس في العلوم وقصده الناس للفتوى . قال المحبى فى خلاصة الأثر : رأس الفقهاء في عصره، كان إماماً فاضلا كبيراً ، حسن السمت جميل ،الطريقة قوى الحافظة، كثير الاطلاع وبالجملة فلم يبق فى آخر أمره من يساويه فى الدرجة . وقد ألف التأليف العجيبة المتقنة :
منها كتابه : تنوير الأبصار" وهو متن فى الفقه جليل المقدار، جم الفائدة، دقق في مسائله كل التدقيق، ورزق فيه السعد، فاشتهر في الآفاق، وشرحه هو الشرح المسمى بـ" منح الغفار" وهو من أنفع كتب المذهب واعتنى بشرحه جماعة منهم : العلامة الحصكفي، مفتى الشام، والملا حسين بن إسكندر الرومى نزيل دمشق، والشيخ عبدالرزاق .
وتوفي رحمه الله في أواخر رجب سنة أربع بعد الألف ١٤٠٤ هـ الموافق ١٥٩٦م
عن خمس وستين سنة .
١١٥- متن الغرر لمنلا خسرو : هو "غرر الأحكام للملا خسرو، محمد ابن فراموز بن علی، متن مشهور عليه شرح للمــاتن باسم الدرر راجع : الدرر
والغرر .
-
١١٦ المجرد : للحسن بن زياد اللؤلؤى ، الإمام، صاحب الإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله . وكان يختلف إلى أبي يوسف وإلى زفر، وله كتاب "المجرد" ولدسنة ٦ ١٦هـ، ومات سنة ٢٠٤هـ .
انظر : الجواهر المضيئة (٥٢/٢) و تاريخ بغداد (٣١٤/٧) .
ولم يذكر صاحب الكشف المجرد للحسن اللؤلؤى . نعم أنه ذكر المجرد في فروع الحنفية لأبي القاسم إسماعيل بن الحسن بن عبد الله البيهقي، اختصر فيه "المبسوط" و "الجامعين" و "الزيادات " ، ثم شرحه وسماه "الشامل"، وللإمام زفر ابن هذيل، وعزاه إلى كتاب الخنثى من بدائع الصنائع للكاساني .
-۱۱۷ مجمع البحرين وملتقى النهرين : مجمع البحرين وملتقى النهرين : هو كتاب جمع فيه مسائل القدوري المنظومة مع زيادات، ورتب فأحسن ترتيبه، وأبدع في اختصاره ، ويذكر في آخر كل كتاب منه ما شذ عنه من المسائل المتعلقة بذلك الكتاب، وهو من تصانيف الشيخ ابن الساعاتي البعلبكي أحمد بن على بن ثعلب البغدادى الجنفي، توفى سنة ٦٩٤
وللزيادة راجع "صاحب المجمع " في الأعلام.
The books mentioned in the sharh by Ibn Mustafa al-Rumi al-Hanafi Afandi, deceased 1070 AH, on al-Durar wa al-Ghurar, in the chapter of mahr.
113 - al-Mabsut al-Kabir: by Shaykh al-Islam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bukhari (deceased 483 AH), known as Bakr Khwarizmi: he is the maternal nephew of the chief judge Imam Abu Thabit Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari. He was among the great scholars of Transoxiana; the famous fatwa books are filled with his mention. He has al-Mukhtasar, al-Tajnis, and al-Mabsut known as Mabsut Khwarizmi, also called al-Mabsut al-Kabir, Mabsut al-Bakri, and Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam. It consists of fifteen volumes.
If you wish more, refer to "Shaykh al-Islam Bakr known as Khwarizmi" in al-A'lam. Note: Also known as Khwarizmi is the scholar Badr al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Kardari, deceased 651 AH, also maternal nephew of Shams al-A'immah Muhammad ibn Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari.
114 - Matn al-Tanwir by al-Timurtashi: It is Tanwir al-Absar wa Jami' al-Bihar. By the scholar Muhammad ibn Abdallah ibn Ahmad al-Khatib ibn Muhammad al-Khatib ibn Ibrahim al-Khatib ibn Muhammad al-Khatib al-Timurtashi, al-Ghazzi al-Hanafi, born in Ghazzah Hashim in 939 AH / 1533 CE. He is called al-Ghazzi, and it is, as in al-Qamus, a town in Palestine. Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) was born there, and Hashim ibn Abd Manaf died there. He may also be called al-Timurtashi.
It is a nisba to Timurtash (with two dammas and a sukun on the ra', a village among the villages of Khwarazm). Al-Shami said the more likely is that it is a nisba to his grandfather Timurtashi. He acquired various sciences in his country from the Mufti of the Shafi'is in Ghazzah, Shams Muhammad ibn al-Mashriqi al-Ghazzi. Then he traveled to Cairo four times and studied fiqh there with Shaykh al-Imam Zayn ibn Nujaym, author of al-Bahr, and the great Imam Amin al-Dawla ibn Abd al-Aal, and studied with Mawla Ali ibn al-Hadha'i, the chief judge of Egypt. He returned to his country as a leader in the sciences, and people sought him for fatwa. Al-Muhibbi said in Khulasat al-Athar: He was the foremost jurist of his time, an imam, virtuous, great, of good appearance, excellent manner, strong memory, vast knowledge; in short, at the end of his life no one equaled him in rank. He authored amazing, precise works:
Among them is his book Tanwir al-Absar, a matn in fiqh of great magnitude, abundant benefit, he scrutinized its issues with utmost precision, and it was blessed with success, so it became famous in all regions. Its sharh is the commentary called Manh al-Ghaffar, which is among the most beneficial books of the madhhab. Many have undertaken to comment on it, including al-Allamah al-Haskafi, Mufti of Damascus, Mulla Husayn ibn Iskandar al-Rumi, resident of Damascus, and Shaykh Abd al-Razzaq.
He died (may Allah have mercy on him) at the end of Rajab in the year 1004 AH / 1596 CE at the age of sixty-five.
115 - Matn al-Ghurar by Mulla Khusraw: It is Ghurar al-Ahkam by Mulla Khusraw, Muhammad ibn Faramuz ibn Ali, a famous matn with a commentary for the texts called al-Durar. See: al-Durar wa al-Ghurar.
-
116 - al-Mujarrad: By al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i, the imam, companion of Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). He used to attend Abu Yusuf and Zufar. He wrote the book al-Mujarrad. He was born in 6? 16 AH and died in 204 AH.
See: al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a (2/52) and Tarikh Baghdad (7/314).
The author of Kashf did not mention al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan al-Lu'lu'i. Indeed, he mentioned al-Mujarrad among the furu' of the Hanafis by Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn al-Hasan ibn Abdallah al-Bayhaqi, who abridged al-Mabsut, al-Jami'ayn, and al-Ziyadat, then commented on it and called it al-Shamil. Also for Imam Zufar ibn Hudhayl, and he attributed it to the book of al-Khuntha from Bada'i' al-Sana'i' by al-Kasani.
-117 - Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn: Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn: It is a book that compiled the masail of al-Quduri in verse form (al-Manzoomah) with additions, and he arranged it excellently and was creative in its abridgment. At the end of each book, he mentions the issues that deviate from that book. It is among the works of Shaykh Ibn al-Sa'ati al-Ba'labakki, Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Tha'lab al-Baghdadi al-Hanafi, who died in 694 AH.
For more, see "Sahib al-Majma'" in al-A'lam.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter listing of key Hanafi reference works cited in the sharh of al-Durar wa al-Ghurar. The author, Ibn Mustafa al-Rumi, enumerates five major texts, providing biographical details about each author and the nature of their work. 

113. al-Mabsut al-Kabir by Bakr Khwarizmi (Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bukhari, d. 483 AH). This is a foundational Hanafi work in fifteen volumes. The author notes alternative names: Mabsut Khwarizmi, Mabsut al-Bakri, Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam. This text belongs to the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus? Actually it's later; but it's a major source of fatwa.  

114. Matn al-Tanwir by al-Timurtashi (Muhammad ibn Abdallah al-Ghazzi al-Timurtashi, d. 1004 AH). This is the matn Tanwir al-Absar wa Jami' al-Bihar, a highly respected text in the Hanafi madhhab. The author studied with Zayn ibn Nujaym (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) and others. His own commentary is Manh al-Ghaffar, and later scholars like al-Haskafi wrote glosses.  

115. Matn al-Ghurar by Mulla Khusraw (Muhammad ibn Faramuz, d. 885 AH?), a famous matn with a commentary called al-Durar. The pair is well-known.  

116. al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i (d. 204 AH), a direct student of Abu Hanifa. This work is a collection of rulings. The passage notes that Kashf al-Zunun did not mention it for him, but it is attributed to a later abridgment by al-Bayhaqi called al-Shamil.  

117. Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn by Ibn al-Sa'ati (Ahmad ibn Ali al-Baghdadi, d. 694 AH). This book compiled the masail of al-Quduri's al-Manzoomah with additions, organized by chapters, and includes deviant issues at the end. It is an important concise reference.

This list is invaluable for students to recognize the sources and chains of transmission within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المبسوط الكبير (al-Mabsut al-Kabir): A major Hanafi fiqh work in fifteen volumes by Bakr Khwarizmi (d. 483 AH), known by various names including Mabsut Khwarizmi and Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam. It is a foundational reference for fatwa.
تنوير الأبصار (Tanwir al-Absar): A well-known Hanafi fiqh matn by al-Timurtashi (d. 1004 AH), also called Tanwir al-Absar wa Jami' al-Bihar. It is known for its precise and comprehensive coverage of masail.
غرر الأحكام (Ghurar al-Ahkam): A matn by Mulla Khusraw (d. 885 AH) on Hanafi fiqh, typically studied together with its commentary al-Durar. The pair is often called 'al-Durar wa al-Ghurar'.
المجرد (al-Mujarrad): A collection of Hanafi rulings by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i (d. 204 AH), a direct student of Abu Hanifa. It is an early source of the madhhab.
مجمع البحرين وملتقى النهرين (Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn): A concise work by Ibn al-Sa'ati (d. 694 AH) compiling the masail of al-Quduri's al-Manzoomah with additions, arranged by chapter, noting deviant issues.

Key Takeaway
The five texts named in this passage—al-Mabsut al-Kabir, Tanwir al-Absar, Ghurar al-Ahkam, al-Mujarrad, and Majma' al-Bahrayn—are essential references in the Hanafi fatwa tradition.

Imam Ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili and His Fatwa Works
Biographical introduction to Ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili and his works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili as the author of al-Mukhtar and al-Ikhtiyar, and state the significance of these texts in the Hanafi fatwa tradition.

Core Idea
One author, two foundational texts: al-Mukhtar and al-Ikhtiyar form the backbone of Hanafi fatwa literature.

This lesson introduces a key figure in Hanafi fatwa literature: Imam Ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili. You will learn about his life, his two major works, and why they are considered reliable references for issuing fatwas. Understanding the authorship and status of these texts is essential for any student of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Find the name of the author, his place of birth (Mosul), and his birth and death years (599–683 AH).
The author is Imam Ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili, a Hanafi jurist.
2
Recognize the two primary works
Note the titles: al-Mukhtar (a concise fatwa manual) and its commentary al-Ikhtiyar. Understand that both were written by the same author.
Al-Mukhtar's full name is 'al-Mukhtar lil-Fatwa'.
3
Understand the relationship between the works
Al-Mukhtar is the matn (base text) and al-Ikhtiyar is its sharh (commentary) written by the same author to explain and substantiate the rulings.
This pairing is common in Hanafi literature.
4
Assess the authority of these books
According to Allamah al-Lakhnawi, both books are considered mu'tabar (reliable) among Hanafi jurists. Recognize this as a mark of their importance.
They are standard references for fatwa.
5
Recognize other commentators
Note that other scholars like Ibn Amir al-Hajj wrote commentaries on al-Mukhtar, and Qasim ibn Qutlubugha extracted its hadith references. This shows the text's widespread acceptance.
Multiple commentaries indicate the value of the original work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتب الواردة في الشرح ابن محمود الموصلى ولد بالموصل سنة تسع وتسعين وخمسمائة (٥٩٩هـ)، وألف "المختار" في عنفوان شبابه، وتمام اسمه "المختار للفتوى ثم صنف شرحا له وسماه بـ الاختيار في تعليل المختار" . مات يوم السبت التاسع عشر من المحرم سنة ثلاث وثمانين وستمائة (٦٨٣هـ ) . قال العلامة اللكنوي هما كتابان معتبران عند الفقهاء . وشرح المختار للعلامة ابن أمير الحاج أيضا، وخرج أحاديثه العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا . وكذلك آخرون كتبوا له شروحا .
The books included in the commentary: Ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili was born in Mosul in the year 599 AH. He authored al-Mukhtar in the prime of his youth, and its full name is 'al-Mukhtar lil-Fatwa'. Then he composed a commentary for it and named it 'al-Ikhtiyar fi Ta'lil al-Mukhtar'. He died on Saturday, the 19th of Muharram, 683 AH. Allamah al-Lakhnawi said: 'Both books are reliable among the jurists.' Also, a commentary on al-Mukhtar by Allamah Ibn Amir al-Hajj, and its hadith were extracted by Allamah Qasim ibn Qutlubugha. And others also wrote commentaries on it.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry introducing Imam Ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili, a prominent Hanafi jurist. It states his birth in Mosul in 599 AH, his authorship of al-Mukhtar (a concise fatwa manual) in his youth, and his later commentary al-Ikhtiyar. The full title of al-Mukhtar is 'al-Mukhtar lil-Fatwa'. The passage then notes that Allamah al-Lakhnawi affirmed both books are authoritative. It also mentions other commentators, such as Ibn Amir al-Hajj who wrote a sharh, and Qasim ibn Qutlubugha who extracted its hadith. This entry serves as a reference for students of Hanafi fiqh to recognize these key texts.

Key Terms
المختار (al-Mukhtar): A Hanafi fatwa text authored by Ibn Mahmud al-Mawsili, known as al-Mukhtar lil-Fatwa.
الاختيار (al-Ikhtiyar): Commentary on al-Mukhtar by the same author, titled al-Ikhtiyar fi Ta'lil al-Mukhtar.

Al-Nihayah: First Commentary on Al-Hidayah by Al-Sighnaqi
Biographical entry with textual clarification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Sighnaqi as the author of al-Nihayah, state its significance as the first commentary on al-Hidayah, and correct the common confusion between al-Nihayah and al-Ayni's al-Binayah.

Core Idea
Al-Sighnaqi’s al-Nihayah is the first and simplest commentary on al-Hidayah; do not confuse it with al-Ayni’s al-Binayah.

This lesson introduces you to Imam al-Sighnaqi, a Hanafi jurist and grammarian, and his monumental work al-Nihayah Sharh al-Hidayah. You will learn why this commentary is important, who its author was, and how to avoid a common mistake in identifying it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its author
Name the commentary (al-Nihayah) and its author (al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Sighnaqi).
The author died in 711 AH.
2
Recognize its place in Hanafi literature
Al-Nihayah is the first known commentary on al-Hidayah, written by a jurist-grammarian.
It is noted as being the simplest and most comprehensive of the early commentaries.
3
Note the author's scholarly credentials
Al-Sighnaqi was a faqih, jadali (dialectician), and nahwi (grammarian). He studied under Hafiz al-Din al-Bukhari and others, and taught at the shrine of Imam Abu Hanifa.
He authored several other works including Sharh al-Tamhid and al-Kafi.
4
Correct the common error
Some mistakenly attribute al-Nihayah to al-Ayni, but al-Ayni's commentary is actually titled al-Binayah.
Al-Ayni explicitly states the title in his introduction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النهاية : النهاية في شرح الهداية أحد شروح "الهداية " بل هو أولها للشيخ الحسين بن على السغناقي الفقيه الحنفى والنحوى الجدلی، توفي سنة ۷۱۱. هي أبسط شروح الهداية وأشملها ، قد احتوى على مسائل كثيرة، وفروع لطيفة، أوله : "الحمد لله الذي أعلى معالم العلوم ... إلخ"، ومصنفه الإمام السغناقي وهو الحسن أو الحسين بن على بن حجاج بن علی حسام الدين السغناقي نسبة إلى "سغناق" (بكسر السين المهملة وسكون الغين المعجمة ثم نون بعدها ألف فقاف) بلدة في تركستان، تفقه على حافظ الدين الكبير محمد بن محمد بن نصر البخاري وفوض إليه الفتوى، وهو شاب وتفقه أيضاً على فخر الدین محمد بن محمد بن إلياس المايمرغى . ومن مصنفاته : شرح التمهيد في قواعد التوحيد ، و الكافي شرح أصول البزدوى"، و "شرح المفصل"، و "النجاح"، و "شرح الهداية المذكور، فرغ عنه في شهر ربيع الأول سنة سبعمائة (٧٠٠) وكان فقيها جدليا نحويا ، أخذ النحو عن العجذوالي [؟]، وغيره . ودخل بغداد ودرس بمشهد الإمام أبي حنيفة، ثم توجه إلى دمشق حاجا فدخلها سنة ٧١٠هـ ، وكان أول من شرح الهداية على مـا ذكـره السيوطي في طبقات النحاة ، وقيل : أول من شرحه حمید الدین علی بن محمد الضرير البخاري، المتوفى سنة سبع وستين وستمائة . وممن تفقه عليه صاحب المعراج وصاحب الكفاية . ذكر صاحب الكشف وفاته عند ذكر "الهداية" ، و "شرح التمهيد"، و "شرح المفصل"، و النجاح"، و "شرح أصول البزدوي ، سنة عشرة وسبعمائة وفيه شبهة، وذكر عند شرح منتخب الإخسيكشي سنة إحدى عشرة وسبعمائة، ونقل في الفوائد عن مدينة العلوم : أنه توفى فى رجب سنة إحدى عشرة وسبعمائة بحلب . ثم اعلم أن صاحب الكشف ذكر النهاية للعيني أيضاً : حيث قال : وشرح القاضي بدر الدین محمود ابن أحمد العيني، المتوفى سنة خمس وخمسين وثمان مائة، الهداية في مجلدات ، وسماه النهاية. انتهى. وهكذا ذكره مولانا عبد الأول الجونفورى فى مفيد المفتى، وهو وهم منهم كما لا يخفى، فإن اسم شرحه البناية (بالباء الموحدة بعدها نون لا النهاية . وقد صرح به العينى فى مقدمة ذلك الشرح .
Al-Nihayah: Al-Nihayah is a commentary on Al-Hidayah, one of the commentaries of Al-Hidayah, indeed it is the first of them, by al-Shaykh al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Sighnaqi, the Hanafi jurist and dialectical grammarian, died in 711 AH. It is the simplest and most comprehensive of the commentaries of Al-Hidayah, containing many issues and subtle branches. Its opening: 'Praise be to Allah who elevated the landmarks of knowledge... etc.' Its author is Imam al-Sighnaqi, who is al-Hasan or al-Husayn ibn Ali ibn Hajjaj ibn Ali Husam al-Din al-Sighnaqi, attributed to 'Sighnaq' (with kasra of the unpointed sin, sukun of the pointed ghayn, then nun followed by alif then qaf), a town in Turkestan. He studied fiqh under Hafiz al-Din al-Kabir Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Bukhari, who delegated fatwa to him while he was young, and also studied under Fakhr al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ilyas al-Maymarghi. Among his works: Sharh al-Tamhid fi Qawa'id al-Tawhid, al-Kafi Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi, Sharh al-Mufassal, al-Najah, and the mentioned Sharh al-Hidayah, which he completed in Rabi' al-Awwal 700 AH. He was a jurist, dialectician, and grammarian; he studied grammar under al-'Ajizawali [؟] and others. He entered Baghdad and taught at the shrine of Imam Abu Hanifah, then traveled to Damascus for Hajj and entered it in 710 AH. He was the first to comment on al-Hidayah according to al-Suyuti in Tabaqat al-Nuhat, and it is said the first to comment on it was Hamid al-Din Ali ibn Muhammad al-Darir al-Bukhari, died in 667 AH. Among those who studied under him are the author of al-Mi'raj and the author of al-Kifayah. The author of al-Kashf mentioned his death when mentioning al-Hidayah, Sharh al-Tamhid, Sharh al-Mufassal, al-Najah, and Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi in 710 AH, with some doubt, and mentioned in Sharh Muntakhab al-Ikhsikthi in 711 AH, and it is transmitted in al-Fawa'id from Madinat al-'Ulum that he died in Rajab 711 AH in Aleppo. Then know that the author of al-Kashf also mentioned al-Nihayah by al-'Ayni, saying: 'The commentary of Qadi Badr al-Din Mahmud ibn Ahmad al-'Ayni, died in 855 AH, on al-Hidayah in volumes, and he named it al-Nihayah.' End. And thus Mawlana 'Abd al-Awwal al-Jawnfuri mentioned it in Mufid al-Mufti, but it is a mistake from them as is not hidden, for the name of his commentary is al-Binayah (with a single ba followed by nun, not al-Nihayah). And al-'Ayni explicitly stated this in the introduction of that commentary.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This is a biographical entry from a list of works (al-Kutub al-Waridah fi al-Sharh) in Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. It describes the commentary al-Nihayah by al-Imam al-Sighnaqi on al-Hidayah. The entry emphasizes that al-Nihayah is the earliest commentary on al-Hidayah, written by a scholar who was both a jurist and a grammarian. It provides details about the author's name, nisbah, teachers, and works. A key point is the correction of a common mistake: some scholars confused al-Sighnaqi's al-Nihayah with al-'Ayni's commentary, which is actually titled al-Binayah, not al-Nihayah. This clarification is important for students referencing these works.

Key Terms
النهاية (al-Nihayah): A comprehensive commentary on al-Hidayah by al-Sighnaqi, considered the first and simplest of its commentaries.
السغناقي (al-Sighnaqi): Al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Sighnaqi, a Hanafi jurist and grammarian, author of al-Nihayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Sighnaqi

Al-Sighnaqi authored al-Nihayah, the first commentary on al-Hidayah; al-Ayni's work is al-Binayah, not al-Nihayah.

Al-Nahr al-Faiq and Its Author Ibn Nujaym al-Saghir
Biographical introduction to al-Nahr al-Faiq and its author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of al-Nahr al-Faiq, state his relationship to Zayn ibn Nujaym, and describe the scope and significance of this incomplete Hanafi commentary.

Core Idea
Al-Nahr al-Faiq is an incomplete yet valued Hanafi commentary by Ibn Nujaym al-Saghir, the younger brother of the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

This passage introduces a key Hanafi reference work, al-Nahr al-Faiq, and its author, 'Umar ibn Nujaym al-Misri (known as Ibn Nujaym al-Saghir). Understanding the lineage of Hanafi commentaries helps you navigate the sources relied upon in fatwa. This entry clarifies the author's relation to the more famous Zayn ibn Nujaym and notes the commentary's incomplete coverage—a critical detail when assessing its authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and author
Read the opening sentence to confirm the full title: al-Nahr al-Faiq Sharh Kanz al-Daqaiq, and the author: 'Umar ibn Ibrahim Siraj al-Din al-Misri, famous as Ibn Nujaym al-Saghir.
The title translates to 'The Superb River: A Commentary on the Treasure of Subtleties'.
2
Note the familial relation
The text explicitly calls him 'the younger brother of the author of al-Bahr' i.e., Zayn ibn Nujaym. This is important for positioning his work relative to the famous al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a comprehensive commentary also on Kanz al-Daqaiq.
3
Recognize the scholarly description
The text praises him as a precise jurist (faqih muhaqqiq), eloquent, and a diver into rare issues. This indicates the high quality of his commentary, despite its incompleteness.
Such phrases signal reliability in the Hanafi tradition.
4
Understand the work's scope
The commentary was not completed—it only reaches the chapter of Judgment (Kitab al-Qada'), section on Imprisonment (Fasl al-Habs). It is preserved in manuscript form.
Incompleteness means it cannot serve as a standalone source for the entire fiqh corpus.
5
Identify other works by the author
He also summarized Anfa' al-Wasa'il by al-Tarsusi into a book called Ijabat al-Sa'il. This shows his broader efforts in the Hanafi tradition.
Summaries like this were often used for easy reference.

Source Text

النهر الفائق شرح كنز الدقائق : هو للعلامة الشيخ عمر بن إبراهيم سراج الدين الشهير بـ عمر ابن نجيم " المصرى، وهو أخ صغير لصاحب البحر زين ابن نجيم وهو فقيه محقق، رشيق العبارة كامل الاطلاع، كان متبحراً في العلوم الشرعية ، غواصا في المسائل الغريبة. توفى سنة خمس بعد الألف (١٠٠٥هـ) ودفن عند شيخه وأخيه الشيخ زين الدين (محبى ملخصاً). وله في النهر مناقشات على شرح أخيه، لكن لم يكمله المانع حدث ووصله إلى كتاب القضاء، فصل الحبس" وهو مخطوط، ولخص أنفع الوسائل للطرسوسي " في كتاب باسم "إجابة السائل " .
Al-Nahr al-Faiq Sharh Kanz al-Daqaiq: It is by the 'Allamah Shaykh 'Umar ibn Ibrahim Siraj al-Din, famous as 'Umar ibn Nujaym al-Misri, and he is the younger brother of the author of al-Bahr, Zayn ibn Nujaym. He is a precise jurist, elegant in expression, complete in knowledge, well-versed in the religious sciences, a diver into rare issues. He died in 1005 AH and was buried near his teacher and brother Shaykh Zayn al-Din (summarized). He has in al-Nahr discussions on his brother's commentary, but he did not complete it due to an obstacle; he reached up to the chapter of Judgment (Kitab al-Qada'), section of Imprisonment (Fasl al-Habs), and it is in manuscript. He summarized Anfa' al-Wasa'il by al-Tarsusi in a book called Ijabat al-Sa'il.

Commentary
This entry describes the commentary al-Nahr al-Faiq on Kanz al-Daqaiq by 'Umar ibn Nujaym al-Misri, commonly known as Ibn Nujaym al-Saghir (the younger). He was the younger brother of the famous Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The text highlights his scholarly abilities and mentions that his commentary includes critical discussions on his brother's work. However, it remained incomplete, only covering up to a section on imprisonment in the chapter of judgements. He also authored a summary of another work. This entry is useful for identifying key Hanafi reference works and their authors.

Key Terms
النهر الفائق (al-Nahr al-Faiq): A commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq by 'Umar ibn Nujaym al-Saghir, known for its incisive discussions.
ابن نجيم الصغير (Ibn Nujaym al-Saghir): Title for 'Umar ibn Nujaym, the younger brother of Zayn ibn Nujaym (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq).
كنز الدقائق (Kanz al-Daqaiq): A matn (text) by Imam al-Nasafi, a foundational work in Hanafi fiqh.

Al-Sadr al-Shahid and His Abbreviation System in al-Waqi'at
Biographical entry with textual notes on compilation method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sources referenced in al-Waqi'at by their abbreviations ('ayn, waw, ba', sin) and apply this system when consulting the text for fatwa research.

Core Idea
Al-Sadr al-Shahid's al-Waqi'at encodes its sources in single-letter abbreviations — decoding them is key to using the work.

Al-Sadr al-Shahid was a towering figure in the Hanafi school. His work al-Waqi'at is not just a collection of legal cases; it is a carefully organized reference that uses a clever abbreviation system to indicate the source of each case. Recognizing these abbreviations allows a mufti to quickly trace the authority behind a ruling. This lesson will help you master that system.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his stature
Read the biographical details to establish the author's credibility and the significance of his work.
Al-Sadr al-Shahid is a major Hanafi authority.
2
Understand the content of al-Waqi'at
The text explains that al-Waqi'at combines four earlier sources: Nawazil of Abu al-Layth, Waqi'at of al-Natifi, fatawa of Abu Bakr, and fatawa of Samarkand.
This makes it a comprehensive collection.
3
Learn the abbreviation system
The author uses single letters: 'ayn = al-Uyun, waw = al-Waqi'at, ba' = Abu Bakr, sin = Samarkand. Memorize these correlations.
The letters are placed near the issues.
4
Apply the system to a sample
Given an example from the text with an abbreviation, state which source it belongs to.
Practice with the letters mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواقعات للصدر الشهيد : هي الواقعات الحسامية : للصدر الشهيد الصدر الماضى الصدر الكبير أبى الصدور، برهان الدين الكبير، ابن مازه برهان الأئمة، حسام الدين أبي محمد عمر بن عبد العزيز بن عمر بن مازه . وهو من أكابر فقهاء الأحناف في القرن السادس. إمام الفروع والأصول، المبرز في المعقول والمنقول، كان من كبار الأئمة وأعيان الفقهاء. له اليد الطولى في الخلاف والمذهب رزق الشهادة في صفر سنة ست وثلاثين وخمس مائة قتله الكافر الملعون بعد وقعة قطعوان بسمرقند ونقل جسده إلى بخارى. وكانت ولادته سنة ثلاث وثمانين وأربعمائة . وكان رحمه الله ،حنفيّا، ومن قال : إنه شافعي فقد توهم . وقد جمع في كتابه "الواقعات " بين "النوازل " لأبي الليث و الواقعات للناطفى، وأخذ من فتاوى أبي بكر محمد بن الفضل، وفتاوى أهل سمرقند . ورتب الكتب كالمختصر المنسوب إلى الحاكم الشهيد، والأبواب كالنوازل، وأشار بالعين إلى مسائل العيون، والواو إلى الواقعات والباء إلى الشيخ أبي بكر، والسين إلى فتاوى سمر قند، فاحفظ و من تصانيفه -١ الجامع الفتاوى الصغرى - الفتاوى الكبرى، -- عمدة المفتى والمستفتي ، ٥ - الواقعات الحسامية ، ٦- شرح أدب القاضي ، ٧ شرح الجامع الصغير . ومخطوطات هذه الكتب موجودة في المكتبات المختلفة. وحفيده میده برهان ... محمود أيضاً كان فقيهاً ماهراً .
Al-Waqi'at by al-Sadr al-Shahid: they are al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya: by al-Sadr al-Shahid, al-Sadr al-Madi, al-Sadr al-Kabir, Abu al-Sudur, Burhan al-Din al-Kabir, Ibn Maza Burhan al-A'imma, Husam al-Din Abu Muhammad Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Umar ibn Maza. He is among the greatest Hanafi jurists of the sixth century. An imam of furu and usul, distinguished in rational and transmitted sciences, he was among the great imams and notable jurists. He had extensive expertise in legal disagreement and the school. He was granted martyrdom in Safar of the year 536, killed by the accursed infidel after the battle of Qatwan in Samarkand, and his body was transferred to Bukhara. His birth was in the year 483. He was, may Allah have mercy on him, Hanafi; whoever said he was Shafi'i has erred. In his book al-Waqi'at he combined the Nawaazil of Abu al-Layth and the Waqi'at of al-Natifi, and took from the fatawa of Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, and the fatawa of the people of Samarkand. He arranged the books like the Mukhtasar attributed to al-Hakim al-Shahid, and the chapters like al-Nawazil, and indicated with 'ayn the issues of al-Uyun, with waw al-Waqi'at, with ba' the Shaykh Abu Bakr, and with sin the fatawa of Samarkand, so memorize. And among his works: 1. Al-Jami' al-Fatawa al-Sughra, 2. Al-Fatawa al-Kubra, 3. 'Umdat al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti, 4. Al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya, 5. Sharh Adab al-Qadi, 6. Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. Manuscripts of these books are found in various libraries. His grandson Mida Burhan ... Mahmud was also a skilled jurist.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on al-Sadr al-Shahid (the Martyr Chief), one of the greatest Hanafi jurists of the 6th Islamic century. His full name and lineage are given, highlighting his honorifics. He was renowned in both furu' (positive law) and usul (legal theory), and excelled in rational (ma'qul) and transmitted (manqul) sciences. He was martyred in 536 AH after the Battle of Qatwan near Samarkand. The text emphasizes that he was definitively Hanafi, correcting any misconception that he was Shafi'i. His book 'al-Waqi'at' (also called 'al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya') is a compilation of legal cases (nawazil) from earlier sources: the Nawazil of Abu al-Layth, the Waqi'at of al-Natifi, the fatawa of Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, and the fatawa of Samarkand scholars. He organized the work like the Mukhtasar of al-Hakim al-Shahid in terms of book arrangement and like al-Nawazil in chapter structure. He used abbreviations: 'ayn for issues from al-Uyun, waw for al-Waqi'at, ba' for Abu Bakr, sin for Samarkand fatawa. This system aids memorization. A list of his other works is provided, including collections of fatawa and commentaries. His grandson Mahmud is also noted as a skilled jurist.

Key Terms
الواقعات الحسامية (al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya): A collection of legal cases (nawazil) compiled by al-Sadr al-Shahid, combining multiple earlier sources.
الصدر الشهيد (al-Sadr al-Shahid): Honorific title for Burhan al-Din al-Kabir, a major 6th-century Hanafi jurist martyred in 536 AH.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Sadr al-Shahid's al-Waqi'at uses a single-letter abbreviation system to indicate the source of each legal case, a tool essential for fatwa research.

Al-Natifi and His Work al-Waqi'at
Biographical entry on al-Natifi and his al-Waqi'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi jurist al-Natifi, state his chain of transmission, and explain the significance of his work al-Waqi'at for the mufti.

Core Idea
Al-Natifi's al-Waqi'at is a rare but essential source of nawazil for the Hanafi mufti.

Al-Natifi (d. 446 AH) is a significant Hanafi jurist whose works on waqi'at (occurring cases) are highly valued. Understanding his place in the chain of Hanafi scholarship helps the mufti trace the authority of rulings. This lesson introduces his biography and his major works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Full Name and Nisba
State the complete name of the jurist: Imam Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Amr al-Natifi al-Tabari. Note the nisba 'al-Natifi' and its origin.
The nisba refers to making or selling a type of sweet (natif).
2
Trace the Scholarly Chain
Identify his teacher (Abu Abd Allah al-Jurjani) and his teacher's teacher (Imam Jassas al-Razi). This connects al-Natifi to the early Hanafi tradition.
Jassas al-Razi is a major early Hanafi authority.
3
List His Major Works
Enumerate the works mentioned: al-Ajnas, al-Ahkam, al-Rawda, al-Furuq (manuscript), al-Waqi'at, al-Nawazil (rare/extant), and al-Hidaya. Note which are extant and which are lost.
Al-Waqi'at and al-Nawazil are rare; al-Hidaya is not the same as al-Marghinani's.
4
Note His Death and Location
Record that he died in Rayy in 446 AH.
This places him in the 5th century AH.

الواقعات للناطفي : هو في مجلد للإمام أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد ابن عمرو الناطفي، الطبرى . والناطفي : نسبة إلى عمل الناطف أو بيعه . وهو على ما ذكره الفيومى نوع من الحلوى ويسمى "القبيطى سمى بذلك لأنه ينطف قبل استضرابه أى يقطر . أخذ عن أبي عبد الله الجرجاني تلميذ الإمام جصاص الرازي . وفي الجواهر المضيئة وهو أحد الفقهاء الكبار، وأحد أصحاب الواقعات والنوازل . ومن تصانيفه الأجناس والأحكام والروضة، والفروق مخطوطة، والواقعات والنوازل نادرة لا توجد وله الهداية، مات بالرى (٤٤٦هـ) سنة ست وأربعين وأربع مائة .
Al-Waqi'at by al-Natifi: it is in one volume, by Imam Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Amr al-Natifi, al-Tabari. And 'al-Natifi' is a relation to the making or selling of natif. Commentary
This passage introduces Imam Abu al-Abbas Ahmad al-Natifi, a Hanafi jurist, and his work 'al-Waqi'at'. The name 'al-Natifi' is derived from a type of sweet (natif), indicating his family's trade. He was a student of Abu Abd Allah al-Jurjani, who was a student of Imam Jassas al-Razi, connecting him to the early Hanafi tradition. Al-Natifi is recognized as one of the major jurists specializing in waqi'at (legal cases) and nawazil (occurrences). His works include several titles, but notably al-Waqi'at and al-Nawazil are rare and no longer extant. He also wrote a work titled al-Hidaya (not to be confused with al-Marghinani's al-Hidaya). His death date is given as 446 AH in Rayy.

Taj al-Shari'a and His Work al-Wiqaya
Biographical entry on Taj al-Shari'a and his work al-Wiqaya

Learning Objective

Core Idea

This lesson introduces a pivotal text in the Hanafi madrasa: al-Wiqaya. Understanding its origin—who wrote it, why, and its relationship to al-Hidayah—gives you a clearer picture of the Hanafi literary tradition. Taj al-Shari'a authored it specifically for his grandson, who later became a major commentator.

This work became a standard textbook in the Hanafi madrasa curriculum.

Al-Walwalijiyya: Authorship and Historical Context
Biographical entry on al-Walwalijiyya with dual attribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts about Abd al-Rashid al-Walwaliji and identify the attribution dispute regarding al-Walwalijiyya.

Core Idea
Al-Walwalijiyya is a major Hanafi fatwa collection, but its authorship is split between two scholars a century apart.

This lesson introduces the fatwa collection known as al-Walwalijiyya. Understanding its authorship and historical background is essential for a mufti who relies on it, as attribution affects the authority of the rulings it contains. The text presents two possible authors, highlighting a common challenge in Hanafi textual history.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary author
The passage first attributes al-Walwalijiyya to Abd al-Rashid ibn Abi Hanifa al-Walwaliji. Note his full name and nisba.
His nisba indicates he is from Walwalij in Badakhshan.
2
Record birth, death, and teachers
Find his birth year (467 AH), death date (after 540 AH), and his teachers: Abu Bakr al-Qazzaz, Muhammad ibn Ali, and Ali ibn al-Hasan al-Burhan al-Balkhi.
3
Recognize the second attribution
The text then cites al-Kashf, attributing al-Walwalijiyya to Ishaq ibn Abi Bakr al-Hanafi (d. 710 AH). Observe the difference in death dates.
This suggests either a different work or a later recension.
4
Understand the connection to Husam al-Din
The second attribution mentions that the work was inspired by Husam al-Din al-Shahid's al-Jami' li Nawazil al-Ahkam, and that Ishaq undertook to detail what Husam al-Din summarized.
This gives context for the work's purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الولوالجية : هي الفتاوى لعبد الرشيد بن أبي حنيفة . قال في الفوائد : عبد الرشيد بن أبي حنيفة بن عبد الرزاق أبو الفتح ظهير الدين الولوالجى (بفتح الواو وسكون اللام ثم الواو المفتوحة ثم الألف ثم لام مكسورة ثم جيم) نسبة إلى ولوالج" مدينة ببدخشان . إمام فاضل نظار كامل تفقه ببلغ على أبي بكر القزاز ، محمد بن علی وعلى بن الحسن البرهان البلخي . وكانت ولادته بولوالج سنة ٤٦٧ هـ، ومات هناك بعد ٥٤٠هـ . وله الفتاوى المعروفة بـ "الولوالجية " . فال الجامع : قال صاحب الكشف : "الفتاوى الولوالجية لظهير الذين أبي المكارم إسحاق بن أبى بكر الحنفى المتوفى سنة (٧١٠هـ) أولها : "الحمد لله الذي جعل العم حجة الإسلام . . . إلخ " ذكر فيها أن الشيخ الإمام حسام الدين الشهيد، كان أشد الناس اهتماماً بتحرير علم الأحكام، فقصر مسافة الطالبين إلى علم الدين بما لخص من حقائقه لا سيما كتابه الجامع لنوازل الأحكام، فاتفق لخادمه المذكور أنه التزم أن يفصل ما أورده
Al-Walwalijiyya: it is the fatawa of Abd al-Rashid ibn Abi Hanifa. He said in al-Fawa'id: Abd al-Rashid ibn Abi Hanifa ibn Abd al-Razzaq, Abu al-Fath Zahir al-Din al-Walwaliji (with fatha on waw, sukun on lam, then waw with fatha, then alif, then lam with kasra, then jim) – a nisba to Walwalij, a city in Badakhshan. He was an imam, virtuous, speculative, complete. He studied under Abu Bakr al-Qazzaz, Muhammad ibn Ali, and Ali ibn al-Hasan al-Burhan al-Balkhi. His birth was in Walwalij in 467 AH, and he died there after 540 AH. He has the fatawa known as al-Walwalijiyya. Then al-Jami' said: the author of al-Kashf said: 'Al-Fatawa al-Walwalijiyya by Zahir al-Din Abi al-Makarim Ishaq ibn Abi Bakr al-Hanafi, died 710 AH. Its beginning: "All praise is due to Allah who made knowledge the proof of Islam..." He mentioned in it that the Imam Shaykh Husam al-Din al-Shahid was the most concerned with editing the knowledge of legal rulings, so he shortened the distance for students to the knowledge of religion by summarizing its truths, especially his book al-Jami' li Nawazil al-Ahkam. So it happened that his mentioned servant undertook to detail what he presented...
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This entry discusses the collection of fatawa known as al-Walwalijiyya. The primary attribution is to Abd al-Rashid ibn Abi Hanifa al-Walwaliji, a Hanafi jurist born in 467 AH in Walwalij (a city in Badakhshan). He studied under notable teachers and died after 540 AH. However, the text then cites al-Kashf, attributing the same work to Ishaq ibn Abi Bakr al-Hanafi, who died in 710 AH. This suggests either multiple works with the same name, a later recension, or a confusion in the source. The excerpt from al-Kashf mentions that the work was inspired by Husam al-Din al-Shahid's al-Jami' li Nawazil al-Ahkam, and that the author (Ishaq) undertook to detail what Husam al-Din had summarized. The passage cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
الولوالجية (al-Walwalijiyya): A collection of Hanafi fatawa, attributed primarily to Abd al-Rashid al-Walwaliji, with a later attribution to Ishaq ibn Abi Bakr.
ولوالج (Walwalij): A city in Badakhshan (modern-day Afghanistan/Tajikistan), the birthplace of the author.

Ibn Wahban and al-Wahbaniyya: A Poetic Summary of Hanafi Fiqh
Biographical entry on Ibn Wahban with caution on fatwa compilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Wahban's contributions to Hanafi fiqh and describe the structure and significance of his work al-Wahbaniyya.

Core Idea
Ibn Wahban's poem al-Wahbaniyya is a concise poetic summary of rare Hanafi rulings arranged by al-Hidayah order.

This lesson introduces you to Ibn Wahban, a Hanafi judge and scholar, and his famous poetic work al-Wahbaniyya. Understanding the provenance and structure of this work is part of the mufti's toolkit, as it compiles rare issues (ghara'ib) in an accessible form. The passage also includes a caution about a fatwa compilation method that appears comprehensive but contains errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his background
Note Ibn Wahban's full name (Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ahmad ibn Wahban al-Dimashqi al-Hanafi), his birth/death (born before 730 AH, died 768 AH), his role as judge in Hama, and his proficiency in fiqh, Arabic, qira'at, and literature.
His biography is quoted from Ibn Hajar's al-Durar al-Kamina.
2
Describe the composition of al-Wahbaniyya
It is a poem (manzumah) on the rare issues of the Hanafi school, arranged according to the order of al-Hidayah. It is also known as 'Qayd al-Shara'id wa Nazm al-Fara'id'. The number of verses is given as a thousand or four hundred.
The poem is taken from thirty-six books and has a commentary by the author.
3
Recognize the significance for a mufti
The passage ends with 'falyahfaz' (so let it be memorized), indicating that this work is a memorization anchor for rare rulings essential for ifta'.
The work is part of the mufti's education.
4
Understand the caution in the passage
The beginning critiques a method that compiles all fatwas from various sources into one book, claiming it contains obvious errors. This warns against superficial comprehensiveness without proper methodology.
This caution is relevant to fatwa collection (rasm al-mufti).

And in it is an apparent error from many aspects, so let one ponder. And these fatwas are manuscript in two volumes. Ibn Hajar said in al-Durar al-Kamina: Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ahmad ibn Wahban al-Dimashqi al-Hanafi, he engaged (in learning) and became proficient and distinguished in fiqh, Arabic, qira'at, and literature, and taught, and became judge of Hama in the year 760 AH until he died in Dhu al-Hijja 768 AH, but he was dismissed in 762 and then reinstated during 763, and he was of praiseworthy conduct. Proficient in fiqh and literature, and he composed his poem on the rhyme of ra' in the meter of tawil of a thousand verses, incorporating in it the rare issues of the Hanafi school, and he commented on it in two volumes, and it is a good and sound poem. And in al-Kashshaf: it is four hundred verses, and he named it 'Qayd al-Shara'id wa Nazm al-Fara'id', taking it from thirty-six books and arranging it according to the order of al-Hidaya, then he wrote a commentary in two volumes and called it 'Uqd al-Qala'id fi Hall Qayd al-Shara'id'. End. And he, may Allah have mercy on him, was born in Dhu al-Hijja before 730. So let it be memorized.

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical sketch of Ibn Wahban and his work al-Wahbaniyya, a poetic summary of Hanafi fiqh. It begins with a critique of a statement made in a commentary that claims to compile a comprehensive book of fiqh and its qawaid by including additional materials. The author (presumably the compiler of this book) says this statement contains obvious errors in many aspects and should be pondered. Then it introduces al-Wahbaniyya as item 152, describing it as a poem by Ibn Wahban. It quotes Ibn Hajar's biographical entry, giving details of his life, his appointment as judge, his dismissal and reinstatement, and his scholarship. The poem is described as containing rare issues of the Hanafi school, originally claimed to be a thousand verses but reportedly four hundred. The work is arranged according to the order of al-Hidaya. The author died in 768 AH. The passage ends with 'falyahfaz' (so let it be memorized), indicating the importance of this work for a mufti.

Key Terms
الوهبانية (al-Wahbaniyya): The poetic composition by Ibn Wahban summarizing rare issues in Hanafi fiqh.
ابن وهبان (Ibn Wahban): Muhammad Abd al-Wahhab ibn Ahmad ibn Wahban al-Dimashqi al-Hanafi, a Hanafi jurist and poet.
قيد الشرائد ونظم الفرائد (Qayd al-Shara'id wa Nazm al-Fara'id): The title of Ibn Wahban's poem, meaning 'The Binding of the Rare Ones and the Stringing of the Unique Ones'.

Biography of Imam al-Nawawi and His Adab al-Fatwa
Biographical introduction to Imam al-Nawawi's work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts of Imam al-Nawawi and explain the significance of his Adab al-Fatwa for Hanafi fatwa training.

Core Idea
Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa sets universal mufti standards, studied across madhhabs including Hanafi.

Before diving into the rules and etiquette of issuing fatwas, we must understand the source and its author. This passage introduces Imam al-Nawawi, a towering Shafi'i scholar whose work on fatwa etiquette is widely used in Hanafi circles. His biography helps us appreciate the authority behind the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and its origin
The passage states that the Adab al-Fatwa is taken from the introduction of Al-Majmu', al-Nawawi's commentary on Al-Muhadhdhab. Understand that this was originally a Shafi'i work but adopted across schools.
Al-Majmu' is a major Shafi'i reference, but the etiquette principles are madhhab-independent.
2
Note key biographical milestones
Extract birth year (631 AH), location (Nawa near Damascus), education (memorized Al-Muhadhdhab quickly), and his dedication to learning (12 daily lessons).
These details establish his scholarly credentials and personal discipline.
3
Understand his scholarly authority
He is described as 'editor and refiner of the Shafi'i school,' a hafiz of hadith, and author of many beneficial works. This makes his writing on fatwa etiquette highly credible.
Even though Shafi'i, his works are respected across madhhabs.
4
Recognize cross-madhhab applicability
The commentator chose this text for a Hanafi audience, indicating that the adab (etiquette) of fatwa is universal. Note the practical takeaway: Hanafi muftis benefit from al-Nawawi's guidance on conduct.
The passage explicitly states the excerpt is used to 'illuminate the path for those afflicted with this trial' of issuing fatwas.

الحمد لله العلي العظيم، والصلاة والسلام على رسوله النبي الأمي الكريم، وعلى آله وأصحابه أجمعين، أما بعد : إن آداب الفتوى التي نحن بصدد التعليقات عليها، مأخوذة من مقدمة "المجموع" للإمام الأجل، شيخ الإسلام محي الدين : أبي زكريا يحيى ابن شرف النووي رحمه الله تعالى ؛ فإنه لما أراد الشروع في شرح المهذب بدأه بالمقدمة في آداب العالم والمتعلم، والمفتى والمستفتي"، وكلامه في ذلك في غاية الحسن والإفادة ونهاية الجودة والبراعة، وهو في الحقيقة لب لباب هذا الباب، ومنتهى الآمال في هذا المجال، ولذا اعتنى أهل العلم بتعليمه للطلاب ليزودوهم قبل سلوكهم طريق العلم بأحسن الآداب، وقام بعض المطابع بإخراج هذه المقدمة مستقلة عن الكتاب، ونحن لما اقتبسنا منها "آداب الفتوى والمفتى والمستفتي" ليكون مصباحًا لآداب الفتوى ونبراسا يضيء السبيل لمن ابتلى بهذه البلوى - يحسن بنا أن نذكر نبذة من ترجمة الإمام النووي، وتعريف شرحه ومتن هذا الشرح ونشير إلى عملنا في التحقيق، فنقول : .

الإمام النووي رحمه الله تعالى هو شيخ الإسلام الحافظ، علم الأولياء، محي الدين، أبو زكريا يحيى ابن شرف الحزامي، النووي. محرّر مذهب الشافعي ومهذبه، ومنقحه ومرتبه، سار في الآفاق ذكره، وعلا في العالم محله وقدره، صاحب التصانيف المشهورة والكتب المباركة النافعة. ولد في العشر الأول من المحرم سنة ٦٣١هـ، وقيل: سنة ٦١٦هـ، بـ "نوا" وهي قرية من الشام من أعمال دمشق. وقرأ بها القرآن، وقدم دمشق وقرأ "التنبيه" في أربعة أشهر ونصف. وحفظ ربع "المهذب" في بقية السنة، ثم لازم كمال الدين المغربي، وبرع في العلوم، حتى صار محققا في فنونه، مدققا في عمله، حافظا للحديث، عارفًا بأنواعه، عليه سكينة ووقار في البحث مع الفقهاء وغيره. وكان لا يضيع وقتاً إلا في وظيفة من الاشتغال، وكان لا يأكل إلا قدراً بعد العشاء، ولم يتزوج قط، وحج مع والده سنة إحدى وخمسين، وحج بعد ذلك حجة أخرى، ومكث قريبا من سنتين لا يضع جنبه على الأرض، وكان يقرأ في اليوم والليلة اثنى عشر درساً على المشايخ في عدة من العلوم. وكان رحمه الله على جانب كبير من العمل، والزهد والصبر على خشونة العيش، وكان لا يدخل الحمام، ولا يأكل من فواكه دمشق؛ لما في ضمانها من الحيلة والشبه. وكان يتقوت بما يأتي من بلدة من عند أبويه. وكان لا يقبل من أحد شيئًا إلا في النادر ممن لا يشتغل عليه فإنه روي أن فقيراً أهدى له إبريقًا فقبله. وكان كثير السهر والتصنيف، وابتدأ في التصنيف في حدود الستين، وتولى دار الحديث الأشرفية بعد أبي شامة سنة ٦٦٥هـ. وتوفى رحمه الله بعد ما زار القدس ليلة الأربعاء، رابع عشر من شهر رجب سنة ٦٧٦هـ، ودفن ببلده رضي الله عنه وعنا [؟].
Praise be to Allah, the High, the Great, and blessings and peace be upon His Messenger, the unlettered noble Prophet, and upon his family and all his Companions. To proceed: Indeed, the Adab al-Fatwa which we are about to comment upon is taken from the introduction of Al-Majmu' by the eminent Imam, Shaykh al-Islam Muhyi al-Din Abu Zakariyya Yahya ibn Sharaf al-Nawawi, may Allah have mercy on him. For when he intended to begin the commentary on Al-Muhadhdhab, he started with an introduction on the etiquette of the scholar and the student, the mufti and the mustafti. His words therein are of the utmost excellence and benefit, and of the highest quality and skill. It is in truth the cream of this subject and the ultimate aspiration in this field. Therefore, the people of knowledge have taken care to teach it to students to equip them with the best etiquette before they embark on the path of knowledge. Some publishers have issued this introduction separately from the book. Since we have excerpted from it 'Adab al-Fatwa wa al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti' to be a lamp for the etiquette of issuing fatwas and a beacon illuminating the path for those afflicted with this trial, it behooves us to mention a summary of the biography of Imam al-Nawawi, a definition of his commentary and the text of this commentary, and to indicate our work in verification. So we say: Imam al-Nawawi, may Allah have mercy on him, is Shaykh al-Islam, the Hafiz, the scholar of the saints, Muhyi al-Din, Abu Zakariyya Yahya ibn Sharaf al-Hizami, al-Nawawi. The editor and refiner of the Shafi'i school, its reviser and organizer. His fame spread across the horizons, and his status and worth rose in the world. He is the author of famous works and blessed beneficial books. He was born in the first ten days of Muharram in the year 631 AH, and it is also said in 616 AH, in 'Nawa', a village in Syria near Damascus. He read the Quran there, then came to Damascus and read Al-Tanbih in four and a half months. He memorized a quarter of Al-Muhadhdhab in the remainder of the year. Then he closely followed Kamal al-Din al-Maghribi and excelled in the sciences until he became a master investigator in his fields, meticulous in his work, a memorizer of hadith, knowledgeable in its types, possessing tranquility and dignity in discussion with jurists and others. He never wasted time except in some occupation of study. He would only eat a little after Isha prayer. He never married. He performed Hajj with his father in the year 651, and thereafter performed another Hajj. He remained for nearly two years without laying his side on the ground. He would read twelve lessons daily to the scholars in several sciences. He was characterized by great action, asceticism, and patience in rough living. He would not enter the bathhouse, nor eat the fruits of Damascus due to the tricks and doubts in their guarantee. He would subsist on what came from his parents from the village. He would not accept anything from anyone except rarely from one who did not study under him; it is narrated that a poor man gave him a jug and he accepted it. He was frequently awake at night and authored works. He began authorship around the age of sixty. He took charge of the Ashrafiyya Dar al-Hadith after Abu Shama in 665 AH. He passed away, may Allah have mercy on him, after visiting Jerusalem, on the night of Wednesday, the 14th of Rajab, 676 AH, and was buried in his town. May Allah be pleased with him and [with us?].
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Nawawi and his work on Adab al-Fatwa. It begins by stating the source: the introduction to Al-Majmu', a major Shafi'i work. The author explains that this excerpt serves as a guide for the etiquette of issuing fatwas. Then follows a detailed biography of Imam al-Nawawi: his birth in Nawa (631 AH), his studies in Damascus, his mastery of Shafi'i fiqh, his asceticism and piety, and his prolific authorship. Notable aspects: he never married, avoided dubious food, and was highly disciplined. He died in 676 AH. This biography is important for understanding the authority behind the Adab al-Fatwa text, which is rooted in the Shafi'i tradition but widely used in Hanafi contexts as well.

Key Terms
الإمام النووي (al-Imam al-Nawawi): Yahya ibn Sharaf al-Nawawi, a leading Shafi'i scholar and author of Al-Majmu' and other works.
آداب الفتوى (Adab al-Fatwa): The etiquette and ethics of issuing fatwas, including the conduct of the mufti and the mustafti.

Imam al-Nawawi: Piety and Authority in Fatwa
Biography of a Shafi'i master with lessons for fatwa ethics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate how the personal piety and scholarly discipline of Imam al-Nawawi lend authority to his fatwa guidelines.

Core Idea
A scholar's life of piety and precision makes his fatwa rulings trustworthy.

This lesson delves into the biography of Imam al-Nawawi, a towering Shafi'i scholar whose works on fatwa etiquette, such as 'Adab al-Fatwa', are foundational. While Hanafi muftis rely on their own madhhab manuals, understanding al-Nawawi's life helps us appreciate the weight carried by his opinions in cross-madhhab discourse. His extreme caution (wara') and relentless pursuit of knowledge set a benchmark for scholarly integrity.

Guided Path
1
Identify Key Biographical Details
Scan the passage for facts about al-Nawawi's birth, education, daily routine, and personal habits. These details paint a picture of his character.
Focus on items that directly relate to his reliability as a scholar, e.g., memorizing 'al-Tanbih' in four months, giving twelve lessons daily.
2
Connect to Fatwa Authority
For each biographical trait, ask: How does this trait support the trustworthiness of his fatwa guidelines? For example, his refusal to eat Damascus fruits due to potential shubha shows extreme caution—a desirable quality in a mufti.
This step bridges character and professional reliability.
3
Reflect on Cross-Madhhab Implications
Why does a Hanafi fiqh manual include a biography of a Shafi'i scholar? Consider that this text ('Rasm al-Mufti' by Ibn Abidin) often cites al-Nawawi for comparative purposes. Understanding his background helps Hanafi muftis contextualize his opinions.
This highlights the value of knowing the source's author.

الإمام النووى رحمه الله تعالى

رجب سنة ٦٧٦هـ ، ودفن ببلده رضى الله عنه وعنابه.
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. 40. Imam al-Nawawi, may Allah have mercy on him, is the Shaykh of Islam, the Hafiz, the scholar of the saints, Muhyi al-Din, Abu Zakariyya Yahya ibn Sharaf al-Hizami, al-Nawawi. Reviser and refiner of the Shafi'i school, his fame spread across horizons, his rank elevated in the world. He authored famous works and blessed beneficial books. He was born in the first ten days of Muharram 631 AH, and some say 616 AH, in 'Nawa', a village in the district of Damascus in Syria. He read the Qur'an there, came to Damascus and read 'al-Tanbih' in four and a half months, and memorized a quarter of 'al-Muhadhdhab' in the remainder of the year. Then he became a disciple of Kamal al-Din al-Maghribi and excelled in the sciences until he became an investigator in his fields, precise in his work, a memorizer of hadith, knowledgeable of its types. He had dignity and gravity in discussions with jurists and others. He did not waste time except in some occupation of learning. He would eat only a small amount after Isha. He never married. He performed Hajj with his father in 651, and later another Hajj. He stayed nearly two years without placing his side on the ground (i.e., avoiding sleep). He would give twelve lessons per day and night to the shaykhs in several sciences. He was on a great level of action, asceticism, patience with rough living. He would not enter the bathhouse, nor eat from Damascus fruits due to the trickery and ambiguity in their guarantee. He sustained himself with what came from his parents in his village. He would not accept anything from anyone except rarely from one who did not study under him—it is narrated that a poor man gave him a jug, and he accepted it. He was often awake and writing. He began authorship around the age of sixty. He took charge of the Dar al-Hadith al-Ashrafiyya after Abu Shama in 665 AH. He passed away, after visiting Jerusalem, on the night of Wednesday, 14th of Rajab 676 AH, and was buried in his town. May Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical sketch of Imam al-Nawawi (d. 676/1277), a towering figure in the Shafi'i school and a major reference for hadith and fiqh. The text emphasizes his status as a reviser of the madhhab, his extraordinary discipline in learning (giving twelve lessons daily), and his extreme asceticism and caution (wara'), such as avoiding Damascus fruits due to potential illicit transactions and refusing gifts except rarely. His authorship of seminal works like 'Riyad al-Salihin' and 'Al-Majmu'' is hinted at. The biography also notes his guardianship of the Dar al-Hadith al-Ashrafiyya, a prestigious institution. This account serves to establish the authority and reliability of al-Nawawi as a scholar whose fatwa guidelines carry weight.

Key Terms
آداب الفتوى (Adab al-Fatwa): The etiquette and rules governing the issuance of legal opinions (fatwa), a genre of works on the conduct of muftis.
النووى (al-Nawawi): Muhyi al-Din Abu Zakariyya Yahya ibn Sharaf al-Nawawi, a leading Shafi'i scholar and hadith master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam al-Nawawi avoid eating fruits from Damascus?
A) He disliked their taste
B) He considered them ritually impure
C) He was cautious due to potential legal ambiguities (shubha) in the transactions
D) He could not afford them

Key Takeaway
A mufti's authority combines knowledge and piety; Imam al-Nawawi embodied both, setting a high standard for trustworthiness in fatwa.
