Lessons from the Biography of Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi for the Mufti
Introduction to the book Al-Muhadhdhab and its author's biography

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key character traits of a classical jurist that inform his authority, and apply this understanding when evaluating references to his works in fatwa contexts.

Core Idea
The mufti's character and method affect the weight of his fiqh, even across madhhabs.

This passage introduces the Shafi'i jurist Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (d. 476/1083) and his seminal work Al-Muhadhdhab. As a Hanafi mufti, you may encounter references to al-Shirazi in fatwa literature or when comparing schools. Understanding his biography helps you assess the reliability and context of his rulings. The passage emphasizes his extreme caution (wara') and rigorous methodology, traits that lend authority to his fatwa tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his school
Note full name: Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Shirazi. He was a leading Shafi'i jurist. For a Hanafi mufti, knowing the madhhab of a cited authority is crucial for proper attribution.
Al-Shirazi belongs to the Shafi'i school, not the Hanafi. His works are referenced in comparative fiqh or when discussing differences.
2
Extract the scholarly method
Al-Shirazi repeated each lesson one hundred times and memorized complete poems for single lines of evidence. This method indicates depth and precision, which enhance the trustworthiness of his legal derivations.
The mufti should consider such diligence as a factor in the authority of the scholar's opinions.
3
Analyze the character traits with legal relevance
The passage highlights asceticism (zuhd), piety (wara'), patience, and avoidance of haste. These traits are not merely personal; they influence how a jurist weighs evidence and makes cautious rulings (ihtiyat).
For a mufti, understanding a scholar's wara' can explain why certain positions lean toward caution.
4
Understand the authority level in the Hanafi tradition
Al-Shirazi is not a primary source in the Hanafi school, but his works are respected as authoritative Shafi'i texts. When a Hanafi mufti cites him, it is usually in a comparative context. His biography shows he is a 'muhaqqiq' (investigator), which elevates the weight of his opinions outside his school.
The mufti should distinguish between 'authority within one's own madhhab' and 'acknowledged expertise across madhhabs.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الفتوى للإمام النووي المهذب :
هو في الفقه الشافعى للشيخ الإمام أبي إسحاق إبراهيم بن محمد الشيرازى، الفقيه الشافعي، الإمام المحقق، المتقن المدقق، ذو الفنون من العلوم المتكاثرات، والتصانيف النافعة المستجادات، الزاهد، العابد، الورع، المعرض عن الدنيا المقبل بقلبه على الآخرة ، الباذل نفسه في نصرة دين الله تعالى، المجانب للهوى، أحد العلماء الصالحين وعباد الله العارفين، الجامعين بين العلم والعبادة، والورع والزهادة ، المواظبين على وظائف الدين، واتباع هدى سيد المرسلين صلى الله عليه وسلم، ورضى عنهم
أجمعين . ولد سنة ثلاث وتسعين وثلاثمائة، وتفقه بفارس على أبي الفرج ابن البيضاوى، وبالبصرة على الخزرى، ثم دخل بغداد سنة خمس عشرة وأربع مائة، وتفقه على شيخه الإمام الجليل الفاضل أبي الطيب طاهر ابن عبد الله بن الطبري، وجماعة من مشايخه المعروفين. وسمع الحديث عن الإمام الفقيه الحافظ أبي بكر البرقاني، وأبي على بن شاذان وغيرهما من الأئمة المشهورين ورأى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في المنام فقال له يا شيخ فكان يفتخر ويقول : سمّانى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم شيخا . قال رحمه الله : كنتُ أعيد كل درس مائة مرة، وإذا كان في المسألة بيت شعر يستشهد به حفظت القصيدة كلّها من أجله ..
وكان عاملا بعلمه، صابراً على خشونة العيش معظما للعلم، مزاعيّاً للعمل بدقائق الفقه والاحتياط. ومن حديثه أنه كان يوما يمشى ومعه بعض أصحابه فعرض في الطريق كلب فزجره ،صاحبه، فنهاه الشيخ وقال : "أما علمت أن الطريق بيني وبينه مشترك " ، ودخل يوما مسجداً ليأكل طعاماً على عادته ، فنسى فيه ديناراً، فذكره في الطريق، فرجع فوجده، ففكر ساعة وقال: "ربما وقع هذا الدينار من غيرى ، فتركه ولم يمسه . قال الإمام الحافظ أبو سعد السمعاني : كان الشيخ أبو إسحاق إمام
The Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi: Al-Muhadhdhab. It is in Shafi'i fiqh by the scholar Imam Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Shirazi, the Shafi'i jurist, the investigating Imam, the precise and meticulous one, possessing multiple sciences, beneficial and excellent writings, the ascetic, the worshiper, the pious, the one turning away from the world with his heart towards the afterlife, the one giving himself in support of the religion of Allah, the one avoiding desire, one of the righteous scholars and the knowledgeable servants of Allah, combining knowledge and worship, piety and renunciation, regular in religious duties and following the guidance of the Master of Messengers, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and may Allah be pleased with them all. He was born in the year 393 AH, studied fiqh in Fars under Abu al-Faraj ibn al-Baydawi, and in Basra under al-Khuzri. Then he entered Baghdad in 415 AH, and studied under his great teacher Abu al-Tayyib Tahir ibn Abd Allah al-Tabari and a group of his well-known shaykhs. He heard hadith from the Imam, jurist, hafiz Abu Bakr al-Barqani, and Abu Ali ibn Shadhan, and other famous imams. He saw the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in a dream, who said to him, 'O shaykh.' he used to boast and say, 'The Messenger of Allah called me shaykh.' He (al-Shirazi) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'I used to repeat every lesson one hundred times, and if there was a line of poetry cited as evidence in an issue, I would memorize the entire poem for its sake.' He was a doer of his knowledge, patient with rough living, magnifying knowledge, and careful to act on the minute details of fiqh and precaution. Among his stories: one day he was walking with some companions, and a dog appeared in the road. His companion scolded it, but the shaykh forbade him and said, 'Do you not know that the road is shared between me and it?' Another day he entered a masjid to eat food as was his habit, and forgot a dinar there. He remembered it on the way, returned and found it. He reflected for a while and said, 'Perhaps this dinar fell from someone else.' So he left it and did not touch it. The Imam, hafiz Abu Sa'd al-Sam'ani said: 'The shaykh Abu Ishaq was an Imam...'
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage introduces the work 'Al-Muhadhdhab' by Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (d. 476/1083), a foundational text in the Shafi'i school. The description extols al-Shirazi's scholarly qualities and his extreme caution and piety. The biography highlights his method of repetition and dedication. An illustrative anecdote about not scolding a dog because the road is shared demonstrates his consideration for the rights of animals. Another about leaving a found dinar due to suspicion it might belong to another reflects his stringent wara'. The text breaks off as al-Sam'ani begins his praise, but the provided portion establishes al-Shirazi's authority as a scholar whose words on fatwa are to be heeded.

Key Terms
المهذب (al-Muhadhdhab): A classic text in Shafi'i fiqh by Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, often studied as a primer.
أبو إسحاق الشيرازي (Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi): Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Shirazi, a leading Shafi'i jurist and teacher in Baghdad.
الورع (al-wara'): Scrupulousness; refraining from doubtful matters to safeguard one's religion.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Caution; taking the safest option in matters of doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He suspected it might belong to someone else, so he left it out of caution
C) He was too busy to retrieve it
D) He thought it was a trap

Key Takeaway
A mufti must distinguish between a scholar's personal piety and his legal rulings, and use biographical information to contextualize, not canonize, a scholar's actions.

The Biography of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi: A Model of Mufti Adab
Biographical account of a scholar's character as a model for muftis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key qualities of a mufti as exemplified by Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi and explain how his practices reflect the adab of ifta'.

Core Idea
Sincerity (ikhlas) is the foundation of a mufti's character; it ensures his knowledge benefits the ummah.

This passage introduces Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, a towering Shafi'i scholar, to illustrate the ethical ideals of a mufti. Although he belongs to another madhhab, his qualities of sincerity, humility, and generosity are universal. Understanding this biography helps us see that adab al-mufti transcends school boundaries and is essential for anyone engaged in ifta'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the virtues
List the personal qualities mentioned in the passage (e.g., asceticism, piety, humility, generosity, eloquence, sincerity). These are the traits of an ideal mufti.
Focus on adjectives like 'zahid', 'wari', 'mutawaddi', 'karim'.
2
Analyze the practices
Identify specific actions that demonstrate adab: praying before writing, eating with companions, leaving food for others, and always bringing intention before giving to the poor.
These actions show that adab is not just theory but practice.
3
Connect to ifta'
Explain how each practice supports the process of issuing fatwa: sincerity ensures rulings are for Allah, humility prevents arrogance, and generosity fosters trust.
Consider how each quality would impact a mufti's interactions with seekers.
4
Note the cross-madhhab lesson
Reflect on why a Hanafi ifta' manual includes a Shafi'i scholar's biography. This shows that adab is common to all schools and that Hanafis can learn from exemplary non-Hanafis.
This is a deliberate pedagogical choice to broaden the student's perspective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى الشافعية، ومدرسا ببغداد في النظامية شيخ الدهر، وإمام العصر، رجل إليه الناس من الأمصار ، وقصدوه من كل الجوانب والأقطار، وكان يجرى مجرى أبي العباس بن سريج . قال : وكان زاهداً، ورعًا، متواضعا متخلفا ظريفا، كريما، سخيّاً، جواداً، طلق الوجه دائم البشر، حسن المجالسة، مليح المحاورة، وكان يحكى الحكايات الحسنة والأشعار المستبدعة المليحة، وكان يحفظ منها كثيراً ، وكان يضرب به المثل في الفصاحة . وكان يكثر مباسطة أصحابه بما سنح له من الرجز، وكان يكرمهم ويطعمهم ، حكى السمعاني : أنه كان يشترى طعامًا كثيراً ويدخل بعض المساجد، ويأكل مع أصحابه، وما فضل قال لهم: "اتركوه لمن يرغب فيه " . وكان رحمه الله ذا نصيب وافر من متابعة الفكر في الله تعالي والإخلاص له، وإرادة إظهار الحق ونصح الخلق، قال أبو الوفاء بن عقيل: شاهدت شيخنا أبا إسحاق لا يخرج شيئًا إلى فقير إلا أحضر النية، ولا يتكلم في مسألة إلا قدّم الاستعانة بالله عزّ وجلّ، وأخلص القصد في نصرة الحق، ولا صنف مسألة إلا بعد أن صلى ركعات، فلا جرم شاع اسمه وانتشرت تصانيفه شرقاً وغرباً ببركة إخلاصه . قلت : وقد ذكر الشيخ أبو إسحاق في أول كتابه "الملخص في الجدل" جملا من الآداب للمناظرة وإخلاص النية وتقديم ذلك بين يدى شروعه فيها، وكان فيما نعتقده متصفاً بكل ذلك. وكتابه "المهذب" كتاب جليل القدر في فقه الشافعي رضي الله عنه ، اعتني بشأنه فقهاء الشافعية، فأول من شرحه على ما قاله اليافعي : أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن منصور العراقي الشافعي، والثاني من الشراح : الشيخ ضياء الدين أبو عمرو عثمان بن عيسى الهدباني، وصنف قريبا من عشرين مجلداً لكن لم يكمله، بل وصل فيه إلى كتاب الشهادة ، وسماه "الاستقصاء المذاهب العلماء والفقهاء"، والثالث : أبو الذبيح إسماعيل بن محمد الحضرمي والرابع : الشيخ الإمام محى الدين أبو زكريا يحيى بن شرف النووى، وشرحه خلق كثير غيرهم.
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. The Shafi'i, and teacher in Baghdad at the Nizamiyya, the elder of the age, and the imam of the era, a man to whom people came from all regions, and they sought him from every side and land, and he was like Abu al-Abbas ibn Suraij. He said: He was ascetic, pious, humble, refined, generous, noble, open-faced, always cheerful, good company, pleasant in conversation, and he would tell good stories and beautiful innovative poems, and he memorized many of them, and he was exemplary in eloquence. He would frequently converse jovially with his companions with whatever meter occurred to him, and he would honor them and feed them. Al-Sam'ani narrated that he would buy a lot of food and enter some mosques and eat with his companions, and what remained he would say to them: 'Leave it for whoever desires it.' He, may Allah have mercy on him, had a great share of reflection upon Allah Almighty, sincerity to Him, desire to manifest truth and advise creation. Abu al-Wafa ibn Aqil said: I witnessed our teacher Abu Ishaq not give anything to a poor person without bringing intention, nor speak on a matter without first seeking help from Allah Almighty, and he would purify his aim in supporting truth, and he would not compose a matter except after praying supererogatory prayers. So inevitably his name became famous and his works spread east and west by the blessing of his sincerity. I said: And Sheikh Abu Ishaq mentioned at the beginning of his book 'al-Mulakhkhas fi al-Jadal' many etiquettes for debate and sincerity of intention and presenting that before embarking upon it, and we believe he was characterized by all of that. And his book 'al-Muhadhdhab' is a book of great status in Shafi'i fiqh, may Allah be pleased with him; Shafi'i jurists paid attention to it. The first to comment on it, according to al-Yafi'i, was Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Mansur al-Iraqi al-Shafi'i. The second commentator: Sheikh Diya al-Din Abu Amr Uthman ibn Isa al-Hadbani, who composed nearly twenty volumes but did not complete it, reaching only the Book of Testimony, and named it 'al-Istiqsa al-Madhahib al-Ulama wa al-Fuqaha.' The third: Abu al-Dhabih Ismail ibn Muhammad al-Hadrami. The fourth: Sheikh Imam Muhyi al-Din Abu Zakariyya Yahya ibn Sharaf al-Nawawi, and many others commented on it.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi (d. 476 AH), a leading Shafi'i jurist and teacher at the Nizamiyya in Baghdad. It emphasizes his personal virtues: asceticism, humility, generosity, and scholarly integrity. The text highlights his dedication to sincerity (ikhlas) and his practice of performing supererogatory prayers before writing. It also mentions his two key works: 'al-Mulakhkhas fi al-Jadal' on the etiquette of debate, and 'al-Muhadhdhab', a foundational Shafi'i fiqh text. The passage lists early commentators on al-Muhadhdhab, including Imam al-Nawawi, whose commentary 'al-Majmu'' is the subject of the next section. Although this biography pertains to a Shafi'i scholar, it is included in a Hanafi ifta' work as a model of adab for muftis and scholars, underscoring the universal importance of ethical conduct and sincere intention.

Key Terms
المهذب (al-Muhadhdhab): The title of a comprehensive work on Shafi'i fiqh by Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi.
الملخص في الجدل (al-Mulakhkhas fi al-Jadal): A work by al-Shirazi on the methodology and etiquette of scholarly debate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The biography of Imam Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi teaches that a mufti's adab—sincerity, humility, and dependence on Allah—is as crucial as his scholarly knowledge.

Life of the Author

Al-Majmu': The Unfinished Magnum Opus of Imam al-Nawawi
Biographical and critical introduction to al-Majmu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the scholarly significance of al-Majmu' and explain why its incompleteness poses challenges for later scholars and muftis.

Core Idea
Al-Majmu' is an unfinished masterpiece that set an unparalleled standard for comprehensive fiqh scholarship.

Imam al-Nawawi's Al-Majmu' was intended to be the ultimate reference for the Shafi'i school, covering not only fiqh but hadith, language, and comparative schools. However, al-Nawawi died after writing only a quarter of the work. This lesson explores the book's ambition, its unfinished state, and why no later scholar could complete it. For a mufti, understanding the authority of such incomplete works is crucial for citing them correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his intention
Read the opening lines to learn the author's name, death date, and stated purpose from the introduction: to make learners independent of all other works and provide definitive knowledge of the Shafi'i school.
Al-Nawawi's intention was not merely to comment on al-Muhadhdhab but to create a comprehensive reference.
2
Assess the scope of the work
Note the areas covered: not only Shafi'i fiqh but also the schools of all scholars, hadith criticism, Arabic language, history, and reconciliation of contradictory hadith.
The text says 'it is a commentary on the schools of all scholars'.
3
Note the evidence of incompleteness
Identify that al-Nawawi only completed about a quarter of al-Muhadhdhab, reaching the chapters on riba. Multiple scholars (Ibn al-Mulaqqin, al-Isnawi, al-Sakhawi) confirm he died before finishing.
Al-Isnawi noted that al-Nawawi seemed aware of his impending death, as he often said 'perhaps we will not reach its place'.
4
Understand why completion failed
Examine the three conditions al-Subki listed as necessary: free time and ample time, access to many books, and good intention/piety. Al-Nawawi possessed all three, while later scholars lacked at least one.
Despite attempts by Ibn al-Attar and al-Subki, no one could complete it.
5
Evaluate the work's enduring value
Consider why al-Majmu' remains a foundational text despite its incompleteness: its methodology, breadth, and the quality of its critical analysis make it indispensable for comparative fiqh and hadith.
The author of al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya said if it were completed, it would have no equal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى المجموع : هو للإمام منحى الدين أبي زكريا يحيى بن شرف النووي، المتوفى سنة ٦٧٦ هـ، وقد شرح به قريبا من ربع المهذب فى تسع مجلدات، وانتهى إلى أبواب الربا . قال صاحب البداية والنهاية : لو كمل لم يكن له نظير في بابه، فإنه أبدع وأجاد وأحسن الانتقاد، وحرر الفقه في المذهب وغيره، والحديث على ما ينبغي، واللغة العربية، ليس في كتب الفقه أحسن منها ، سلك طريقة مهذبة حسنة سهلة جمعت أشتات عيون المسائل، ومذاهب العلماء ومفردات الفقهاء، وتحرير الألفاظ، ومسالك الأئمة الفقهاء، وبيان صحة الحديث من سقمه ومشهوره من عكسه. أراد به النووى كما قال في المقدمة - : " أن يستغنى بالمجموع عن كل مصنف، ويعلم به مذهب الشافعى علما قطعيا . ولقد وفقه الله لما أراد فهو ليس شرحًا للمهذب، بل لمذاهب العلماء كلهم، وللحديث، واللغة، والتاريخ، والأسماء، وهو أصل عظيم في معرفة صحيح الحديث وحسنه وضعيفه، وبيان علله ، والجمع بين الأحاديث المتعارضات، وتأويل الخفيات، واستنباط المهمات . قال ابن الملقن: "مات ولم يكمله ، وليته أكمله وانخرمت باقى كتبه . قال الأسنوى : " وهذا الشرح من أجل كتبه وأنفسها، وكلامه فيه يدل على أنه اطلع على أنه يموت قبل إتمامه، فإنه يجمع النظائر في موضع ويقول معلنا ذلك : فلعلنا لا نصل إلى محله " . وقيل : إن الإمام النووى أو عد لتلميذه ابن العطار، إذا قدرت له الوفاة أن يتمه ، ودفع إليه ورقة عين مواده فيه ؛ ليكمل شرح المهذب، ولم يقدر لابن العطار ذلك . وقال السخاوى : " ولم يتهيأ لأحد إتمامه " ونقل في تهذيب الأسماء واللغات عن ابن العطار أنه قال : وكتب لي ورقة فيها أسماء الكتب التي كان يجمعه منها وقال: "إذا انتقلت إلى الله فأتمه آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى من هذه الكتب A.. .وقد شرع في تكميله جماعة ولم ينهوه، فكتب الشيخ تقي الدين السبكى من الموضع الذي انتهى إليه . وقال في خطبة تكملته واصفا هذا الشرح: وبعد: فقد رغب إلى بعض الأصحاب في أن أكمل شرح المهذب للشيخ الإمام العالم العلامة ، علم الزهّاد وقدوة العباد، واحد عصره وفريد دهره، محيى علوم الأولين ومهذب سنن الصالحين، أبي زكريا النووي. وطالت رغبته إلى، وكثر إلحاحه على وأنا في ذلك أقدم رجلا وأأخر أخرى، وأستهول الخطب وأراه شيئًا إمراً، وهو في ذلك لا يقبل عُذراً، وأقول وقديكون تعرضى لذلك مع قصورى عن مقام هذا الشارح إساءة إليه، وجناية منى عليه، فإنّني أنهض بما ننهض به وقد أسعف بالتأييد وساعدته المقادير فقربت منه كل بعيد. ولا شك أن ذلك يحتاج بعد الأهلية إلى ثلاثة أشياء : أحدها فراغ البال واتساع الزمان. وقد كان رحمه الله قد أوتي من ذلك الحظ الأوفر ، بحيث لم يكن له شاغل عن ذلك من نفس ولا أهل . الثاني : جمع الكتب التي استعان بها على النظر والاطلاع على كلام العلماء، وكان رحمه الله قد حصل له من ذلك حظ وافراً ؛ لسهولة ذلك في بلده في ذلك الوقت. الثالث : حُسن النية وكثرة الورع والزهد والأعمال الصالحة التي أشرقت أنوارها، وكان قد اكتال من ذلك بالمكيال الأوفى. فمن اجتمعت فيه هذه الحالات الثلاث أنّى يضاهيه أو يدانيه من ليس فيه واحدة منها. فنسأل الله أن يُحسن نياتنا ، وأن يمدنا بمعونته وعونه، وقد استخرت الله تعالى وفوضت الأمر إليه، واعتمدت في كل الأمور عليه، وقلت في نفسي : لعلّ ببركة صاحبه ونيته يعيننى الله تعالى عليه، إنه يهدى من يشاء إلى صراط مستقيم، فإن من الله تعالى بإكماله، فلا شك من فضل الله بركة صاحبه ونيته، إذ كان مقصوده النفع للناس ممن كان . تهذيب الأسماء واللغات : ١٦/١، ١٧)
Etiquette of Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi, Al-Majmu': It is by Imam Muhyi al-Din Abu Zakariya Yahya bin Sharaf al-Nawawi, died in 676 AH. He commented on nearly a quarter of al-Muhadhdhab in nine volumes, and ended at the chapters of Riba. The author of al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya said: If it were completed, it would have no equal in its field, for he was innovative, excellent, and good at criticism; he refined fiqh in the madhhab and others, hadith as it should be, and Arabic language. There is no better book among fiqh books. He followed a refined, good, easy method that collected scattered gems of issues, the schools of scholars, the individual opinions of jurists, precise wording, the paths of leading jurists, and clarification of the authenticity of hadith, its weakness, its famous from its opposite. Al-Nawawi intended by it, as he said in the introduction: 'That one should be independent of all other works by Al-Majmu', and learn the Shafi'i school definitively.' And Allah granted him success in what he intended, for it is not a commentary on al-Muhadhdhab alone, but on the schools of all scholars, on hadith, language, history, and names. It is a great foundation for knowing authentic, good, and weak hadith, explaining its defects, reconciling contradictory hadith, interpreting obscure ones, and deriving important matters. Ibn al-Mulaqqin said: 'He died without completing it, would that he had completed it, and his remaining books were lost.' Al-Isnawi said: 'This commentary is among his greatest and finest works, and his words in it indicate that he knew he would die before completing it, for he gathers analogous cases in one place and says, announcing that: Perhaps we will not reach its place.' It is said that Imam al-Nawawi instructed his student Ibn al-Attar, if death overtook him, to complete it, and gave him a paper specifying its sources to complete the commentary on al-Muhadhdhab, but Ibn al-Attar was not able to do so. Al-Sakhawi said: 'No one was able to complete it.' It was transmitted in Tahdhib al-Asma' wa al-Lughat from Ibn al-Attar that he said: 'He wrote for me a paper containing the names of the books from which he used to compile, and said: When I depart to Allah, complete it from these books. A group began to complete it but did not finish it. Then Shaykh Taqi al-Din al-Subki wrote from where he stopped. He said in the preface of his completion describing this commentary: After, some companions requested that I complete the commentary on al-Muhadhdhab by the Imam, the scholar, the sign, the knowledge of ascetics and the model of worshippers, the unique of his age and the peerless of his time, the reviver of the sciences of the predecessors and the refiner of the ways of the righteous, Abu Zakariya al-Nawawi. His desire to me prolonged and his insistence increased, while I was hesitating, considering the matter difficult and seeing it as a serious thing. But he did not accept excuses. I say: Perhaps my engaging in this, despite my inadequacy compared to this commentator, is an offense against him and a crime on my part, for I am undertaking what I cannot carry. But he was supported by divine aid, and destiny assisted him, bringing close every distant thing. Undoubtedly, this, after qualification, requires three things: First, free time and ample time. He, may Allah have mercy on him, was given the greatest share of that, such that he had no distraction from it, neither self nor family. Second, collecting the books he used for study and reviewing the words of scholars. He had ample share of that due to ease in his town at that time. Third, good intention, abundant piety, asceticism, and righteous deeds whose lights shone. He had taken from that with the fullest measure. So when these three qualities are combined in a person, how can anyone who lacks even one of them equal or approach him? So we ask Allah to improve our intentions, and to aid us with His help and support. I prayed istikhara to Allah and entrusted the matter to Him, relying on Him in all matters, and said to myself: Perhaps through the blessing of its author and his intention, Allah will help me with it. Indeed, He guides whom He wills to a straight path. So its completion is from Allah, and there is no doubt of Allah's grace, the blessing of its author and his intention, since his purpose was benefit to people. Tahdhib al-Asma' wa al-Lughat: 16/1, 17)
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and critical introduction to one of the most celebrated works in Shafi'i fiqh, Imam al-Nawawi's 'Al-Majmu'. The text first identifies the author—Imam Muhyi al-Din Abu Zakariya Yahya ibn Sharaf al-Nawawi (d. 676 AH)—and describes the scope of his unfinished commentary on al-Muhadhdhab. It praises the book's comprehensive methodology, which covers not only the Shafi'i school but the positions of all scholars, hadith criticism, Arabic language, and reconciliation of conflicting evidence. The core idea is that al-Nawawi intended this book to be a self-sufficient reference, but he died before completing it, reaching only the chapters on riba. The passage then recounts several scholars' assessments: Ibn al-Mulaqqin lamented its incompleteness, al-Isnawi noted that al-Nawawi seemed aware of his impending death, and al-Sakhawi stated that no one managed to finish it. It also mentions that al-Nawawi gave his student Ibn al-Attar a list of sources to complete the work, but Ibn al-Attar was unable. Finally, the text quotes Shaykh Taqi al-Din al-Subki, who attempted a completion, explaining the need for free time, access to books, and sincere intention—qualities he saw abundantly in al-Nawawi. This passage serves to highlight the high standard of scholarship represented by al-Majmu' and the difficulty of matching it, even for later scholars.

Key Terms
المجموع (Al-Majmu'): The comprehensive commentary by Imam al-Nawawi on al-Muhadhdhab, intended to cover all schools of thought and become the definitive Shafi'i reference.
المهذب (Al-Muhadhdhab): A foundational text in Shafi'i fiqh by Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, which al-Nawawi commented on in al-Majmu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Nawawi state about the purpose of al-Majmu' in his introduction?
A) To summarize the main points of al-Muhadhdhab
B) To make one independent of all other works and teach the Shafi'i school definitively
C) To critique the Hanafi school
D) To provide a simple guide for beginners

Key Takeaway
Al-Majmu' is an unfinished but methodologically groundbreaking work that remains a benchmark for comprehensive fiqh scholarship, and its incompleteness is a testament to the exceptional conditions required for such a task.

Al-Subki's Completion of Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: Scholarly Ethics in Fiqh Commentary
Biographical account of scholarly completion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Subki's three prerequisites for completing a major commentary and evaluate their relevance to modern fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Completing a great scholar's work requires tranquility, resources, and piety — not just knowledge.

This passage from the editorial introduction to 'Adab al-Fatwa' recounts how Shaykh Taqi al-Din al-Subki, after much hesitation, agreed to complete Imam al-Nawawi's unfinished commentary on al-Muhadhdhab. In his preface, al-Subki outlines three essential conditions that enabled al-Nawawi to produce such a monumental work and that anyone attempting a similar task must possess. These conditions—mental space, access to books, and sincerity—are timeless lessons for any scholar embarking on a major fiqh project.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Understand that al-Subki is completing al-Nawawi's Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, a major Shafi'i commentary. Recognize that this is a biographical passage about scholarly succession.
The text is from the introduction to al-Subki's completion.
2
List the three prerequisites
Extract the three conditions al-Subki mentions: (1) farāgh al-bāl (free mind) and ittisāʿ al-zamān (ample time), (2) jamʿ al-kutub (collection of books needed for research), (3) ḥusn al-niyyah (good intention), waraʿ (piety), zuhd (asceticism), and aʿmāl ṣāliḥa (righteous deeds).
These are found in the Arabic passage after 'thalāthat ashyā':'.
3
Explain each prerequisite
First: a scholar must have mental tranquility and sufficient time, free from distractions of self or family. Second: access to necessary books and scholarly works. Third: sincere intention, piety, and righteous deeds. Al-Subki emphasizes al-Nawawi possessed these abundantly.
Al-Subki uses the metaphor of 'the fullest measure' for al-Nawawi's virtues.
4
Reflect on al-Subki's hesitation and resolution
Al-Subki initially hesitated due to feeling inadequate compared to al-Nawawi. He resolved through istikhāra, reliance on God, and hope for blessing through al-Nawawi's intention. This shows scholarly humility and trust in divine assistance.
He says: 'I put forward one foot and pulled back the other.'
5
Consider relevance for today's mufti
A contemporary mufti embarking on a major project (e.g., a comprehensive fatwa on a new issue) should assess whether they have these three conditions. Without them, the work may be flawed. This passage serves as a model for scholarly ethics.
Apply to modern scenarios like issuing fatwas on complex financial matters.

آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى
من هذه الكتب
A..
.وقد شرع في تكميله جماعة ولم ينهوه، فكتب الشيخ تقي الدين السبكى من الموضع الذي انتهى إليه . وقال في خطبة تكملته واصفا هذا الشرح:
وبعد: فقد رغب إلى بعض الأصحاب في أن أكمل شرح المهذب للشيخ الإمام العالم العلامة ، علم الزهّاد وقدوة العباد، واحد عصره وفريد دهره، محيى علوم الأولين ومهذب سنن الصالحين، أبي زكريا النووي. وطالت رغبته إلى، وكثر إلحاحه على وأنا في ذلك أقدم رجلا وأأخر أخرى، وأستهول الخطب وأراه شيئًا إمراً، وهو في ذلك لا يقبل عُذراً، وأقول وقديكون تعرضى لذلك مع قصورى عن مقام هذا الشارح إساءة إليه، وجناية منى عليه، فإنّني أنهض بما ننهض به وقد أسعف بالتأييد وساعدته المقادير فقربت منه كل بعيد. ولا شك أن ذلك يحتاج بعد الأهلية إلى ثلاثة أشياء : أحدها فراغ البال واتساع الزمان. وقد كان رحمه الله قد أوتي من ذلك الحظ الأوفر ، بحيث لم يكن له شاغل عن ذلك من نفس ولا أهل . الثاني : جمع الكتب التي استعان بها على النظر والاطلاع على كلام العلماء، وكان رحمه الله قد حصل له من ذلك حظ وافراً ؛ لسهولة ذلك في بلده في ذلك الوقت. الثالث : حُسن النية وكثرة الورع والزهد والأعمال الصالحة التي أشرقت أنوارها، وكان قد اكتال من ذلك بالمكيال الأوفى. فمن اجتمعت فيه هذه الحالات الثلاث أنّى يضاهيه أو يدانيه من ليس فيه واحدة منها. فنسأل الله أن يُحسن نياتنا ، وأن يمدنا بمعونته وعونه، وقد استخرت الله تعالى وفوضت الأمر إليه، واعتمدت في كل الأمور عليه، وقلت في نفسي : لعلّ ببركة صاحبه ونيته يعيننى الله تعالى عليه، إنه يهدى من يشاء إلى صراط مستقيم، فإن من الله تعالى بإكماله، فلا شك من فضل الله بركة صاحبه ونيته، إذ كان مقصوده النفع للناس ممن كان . تهذيب الأسماء واللغات : ١٦/١، ١٧)
Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. From these books. Some people began completing it but did not finish it. So Shaykh Taqi al-Din al-Subki wrote from where he (al-Nawawi) left off. And he said in the introduction to his completion, describing this commentary: 'After praise of God: Some of my companions requested that I complete the commentary on al-Muhadhdhab of the shaykh, the imam, the scholar, the all-knowing, the ornament of ascetics and model of worshippers, the unique of his age and peerless of his time, reviver of the sciences of the predecessors and refiner of the ways of the righteous, Abu Zakariyya al-Nawawi. His request prolonged, and his insistence increased upon me, while I would put forward one foot and pull back the other, and I considered the matter great and I saw it as something serious, but he would not accept any excuse. I said to myself: perhaps my venturing into this, despite my inadequacy compared to the stature of this commentator, would be an offense to him and a crime against him. I cannot do what I cannot do. But (God) assisted with support, and fate aided me, bringing every distant thing near. There is no doubt that this, after competence, requires three things: first, a free mind and ample time. He (al-Nawawi) was given the greatest share of that, so that he had no distraction from it, neither from himself nor from family. Second, the collection of books he used for research and reviewing the utterances of scholars. He was given a large share of that, due to the ease of obtaining them in his town at that time. Third, good intention, abundant piety, asceticism, and righteous deeds whose lights shone. He had taken from that with the fullest measure. So whoever combines these three states, how can someone who lacks even one of them match or approach him? So we ask God to improve our intentions and to grant us His help and assistance. I have asked God for guidance and delegated the matter to Him, and I rely on Him in all things. I said to myself: perhaps through the blessing of its author and his intention, God will help me in it. Indeed, He guides whom He wills to a straight path. For the completion was indeed from God, by His virtue, the blessing of its author and his intention, since his aim was to benefit people.' (Source: Tahdhib al-Asma wa al-Lughat 16/1, 17)
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage from the editorial introduction to 'Adab al-Fatwa' of Imam al-Nawawi presents the biographical account of how Shaykh Taqi al-Din al-Subki (d. 756 AH) undertook the completion of al-Nawawi's commentary on al-Muhadhdhab, a major Shafi'i fiqh text. The author of this introduction quotes al-Subki's own description from the preface of his completion. Al-Subki explains that he was initially reluctant due to his perceived inadequacy compared to al-Nawawi, but after persistent requests from colleagues and reliance on God, he began. He enumerates three essential prerequisites for such a scholarly undertaking: (1) mental tranquility and ample time, (2) access to necessary books, and (3) sincerity, piety, and righteous deeds. He emphasizes that al-Nawawi possessed these abundantly. This account serves as a model for scholarly ethics and the recognition of one's limitations while trusting in divine support. It also highlights the reverence for al-Nawawi and the importance of completing unfinished scholarly works.

Key Terms
تكملة (takmila): Completion or supplement of a scholarly work left unfinished by its author.
المهذب (al-Muhadhdhab): A famous Shafi'i fiqh text by Imam al-Shirazi, upon which al-Nawawi wrote a commentary (Sharh al-Muhadhdhab).
فراغ البال (farāgh al-bāl): Free mind, mental tranquility, undistracted by worldly concerns.
حسن النية (ḥusn al-niyyah): Good intention, sincerity in seeking Allah's pleasure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti
C) Abd al-Karim al-Rafi'i
D) Ibn al-Salah

Key Takeaway
The success of a scholarly work depends not only on knowledge but on conducive conditions and sincere intention before Allah.

Biographical Index: Ibn Abi Layla and Ibn Burhan in Adab al-Fatwa
Biographical entries for key scholars from Adab al-Fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the biographical significance of Ibn Abi Layla and Ibn Burhan in the context of Hanafi fatwa literature and explain why such biographical entries are included in Adab al-Fatwa.

Core Idea
Biographical entries in fatwa manuals establish the authority and reliability of cited scholars.

This passage from Imam al-Nawawi's Adab al-Fatwa provides biographical sketches of two key scholars frequently referenced in fatwa works. Understanding their background helps a mufti evaluate the weight of their opinions. While not a ruling itself, this index is crucial for assessing the chain of authority in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholars and their madhhab affiliations
Read the entry for each scholar and note their name, nickname, and school (madhhab). Ibn Abi Layla is a tabi'i and early Kufan jurist, not strictly a Hanafi but a predecessor. Ibn Burhan started Hanbali and became Shafi'i; he is an usuli scholar.
Ibn Abi Layla's madhhab is not explicitly stated; he is a tabi'i whose views are cited in ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the sources used in their biographies
The text cites references like Tahdhib al-Kamal and Siyar A'lam al-Nubala'. These are authoritative biographical works that authenticate the details provided.
Knowing the source helps assess the reliability of the biography itself.
3
Evaluate the indicators of scholarly authority
For Ibn Abi Layla, the text mentions him encountering many Companions, his circle being respected, and his use of Qur'an to answer questions. For Ibn Burhan, his teachers (al-Ghazali), his usul works, and his reputation in solving problems establish authority.
These indicators help a mufti trust the scholar's opinions.
4
Reflect on why a mufti needs this biographical context
A mufti must know the background of cited scholars to correctly weigh their opinions in fatwa. For example, Ibn Burhan's Shafi'i affiliation means his usul views may differ from Hanafi ones, and knowing that prevents misapplication.
This step connects biography to fatwa methodology.

فهر من الأعلام
١٠٣ آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى
التعريف
بالأعلام الواردة فى آداب الفتوى للإمام النووى
-١ ابن أبي ليلى : هو عبد الرحمن بن يسار المعروف بابن أبي ليلى الأنصارى، الأوسى، أبو عيسى، الكوفي، من أجلة التابعين . قال عطاء بن السائب، عن عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلي : " أدركت عشرين ومائة من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كلهم من الأنصار، إذا سئل أحدهم عن شيء أحب أن يكفيه صاحبه". قال عبدالملك بن عمير : "لقد رأيت عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى في حلقة فيها نفر من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يستمعون الحديثه وينصتون له فيهم البراء بن عازب . قال محمد بن سيرين : جلست إلى عبد الرحمن ابن أبي ليلى، وأصحابه يعظمونه كأنه أمير " . قال ثابت البناني : "كنا إذا قعدنا إلى عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى قال لرجل : اقرأ القرآن، فإنه يدلني على ما تريدون، نزلت هذه الآية كذا"، وهذه الآية كذا. مات سنة ٨٣/٨٢هـ . (راجع : تهذيب الكمال : ٣٥٢/١١، وسير أعلام النبلاء : ٢٤٥/٥)
- ابن برهان : هو أبو الفتح أحمد بن على بن برهان (بفتح الباء) الحنبلي ثم الشافعي، ولد ببغداد في شوال سنة تسع وسبعين وأربع مائة، وتفقه على الغزالي، والكيا، والشاشي وبرع في المذهب، وفي الأصول، وكان هو الغالب عليه، وله فيه التصانيف المشهورة : "البسيط" و "الوسيط" و "الوجيز" وغيرها . رحل إليه الطلبة . من البلاد، واستغرق نهاره وبعض ليله في إقرائهم، ودرس بالنظامية شهراً ثم عزل، وكان ذكيا يضرب به المثل في حل الإشكال، توفى سنة عشرين وخمسمائة، وقيل: غير ذلك. (طبقات الشافعية للإسنوى : ٢٠٧/١)
Index of notable figures. 103 Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. Identification of the notable figures mentioned in Adab al-Fatwa by Imam al-Nawawi. 1. Ibn Abi Layla: He is Abd al-Rahman ibn Yasar, known as Ibn Abi Layla al-Ansari, al-Awsi, Abu Isa, al-Kufi, one of the great Followers. Ata ibn al-Sa'ib said, from Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla: 'I encountered one hundred and twenty of the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him), all of them from the Ansar; when one of them was asked about something, he wished that his companion would suffice him.' Abd al-Malik ibn Umayr said: 'I saw Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla in a circle containing a number of the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) listening to his hadith and paying attention to him, among them al-Bara' ibn Azib.' Muhammad ibn Sirin said: 'I sat with Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, and his companions honored him as if he were a prince.' Thabit al-Bunani said: 'When we sat with Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla, he would say to a man: Recite the Qur'an, for it indicates to me what you want; this verse was revealed concerning such-and-such, and this verse concerning such-and-such.' He died in the year 82/83 AH. (Reference: Tahdhib al-Kamal 11/352, and Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' 5/245). 2. Ibn Burhan: He is Abu al-Fath Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Burhan (with a fatha on the ba') al-Hanbali then al-Shafi'i. He was born in Baghdad in Shawwal of the year 479 AH. He studied fiqh under al-Ghazali, al-Kiya, and al-Shashi, excelled in the madhhab and in usul, and the latter was dominant over him. He authored famous works in usul: al-Basit, al-Wasit, al-Wajiz, and others. Students traveled to him from various lands. He devoted his daytime and part of his night to teaching them. He taught at the Nizamiyya for a month and then was dismissed. He was intelligent and proverbial in solving problems. He died in the year 520 AH, and it is said otherwise. (Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya by al-Isnawi: 1/207).
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a biographical index from 'Adab al-Fatwa' by Imam al-Nawawi. The text provides background on two scholars frequently cited in the work. Ibn Abi Layla was a prominent tabi'i known for his vast knowledge and respect among the Companions, often using the Qur'an to deduce rulings. Ibn Burhan was a later Hanbali-turned-Shafi'i jurist and usuli, a student of al-Ghazali, known for his works on usul al-fiqh. Such biographical entries help readers understand the authority and context of the scholars referenced in the fatwa manual.

Key Terms
ابن أبي ليلى (Ibn Abi Layla): Abd al-Rahman ibn Yasar, a prominent tabi'i and jurist from Kufa, known for his knowledge of Qur'anic exegesis and fiqh.
ابن برهان (Ibn Burhan): Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Burhan, a Shafi'i usuli scholar, author of works on usul al-fiqh like al-Basit and al-Wasit.
